Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Compensating Deficiency in Wajib Acts: The Hanafi Principle of Jabr al-Nuqsan
Explaining the rule of compensating deficiency with examples and a dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of jabr al-nuqsan (compensating deficiency) to determine whether a deficiency in a wajib act is compensated by its like or dropped, and identify the role of istihsan in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A deficiency in a wajib act is compensated by its like if possible; otherwise, the ruling drops but sin remains.

In Hanafi usul, not every deficiency in an obligatory act invalidates it. The Lawgiver has designated certain acts as compensations (such as sajdat al-sahw for prayer or dam for hajj) to fill the gap. This lesson explores when a deficiency can be made up by a like (mithl) and when it is simply dropped, with the crucial exception of sin. We also examine a key dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn regarding compensation for quality when a false coin is paid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wajib act and the deficiency
First determine which act is wajib (obligatory but not fard) and what deficiency occurred (e.g., leaving a wajib or performing it imperfectly).
Wajib acts include things like recitation of al-Fatiha, qunut, tashahhud, and takbirs of Eid.
2
Check if a mithl (like) exists for the deficiency
A mithl can be rational (like performing a similar act) or legal (like sajdat al-sahw or dam). The passage states three types: reasonable in form and meaning, reasonable in meaning only, or not reasonable but legally considered compensatory.
Example: The attribute of moderation in pillars has no like independent of the original act.
3
Apply the rule: if mithl exists, compensate; otherwise drop
If a like exists (e.g., sajdat al-sahw for leaving qira'at al-Fatiha), the deficiency is compensated and the act is complete. If no like exists (e.g., ta'dil al-arkan in prayer), the deficiency is dropped, but the person is still sinful.
The ruling of deficiency is dropped, meaning the act is considered valid, but sin remains because the wajib was not fulfilled perfectly.
4
Analyze the coin dispute: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa argues the attribute of quality (joodah) has no separate like, so if a false coin perishes, the debtor owes nothing (analogy). The Sahibayn argue using istihsan: the creditor's right to quality must be preserved, so the debtor should pay a like of the coin.
The commentary notes that Abu Hanifa's qiyas is stronger because the attribute cannot be separated, but the Sahibayn's istihsan aims to protect the creditor's right.

Source Text

فصل الواجب بحكم الأمر نوعان
إن أمكن جبر النقصان بالمثل ينجبر به وإلا يسقط حكم النقصان إلا في الإثم.
وعلى هذا إذا ترك تعديل الأركان في باب الصلاة لا يمكن تداركه بالمثل عقلا ولا شرعا. إذ لا مثل له عند العبد فسقط حكم النقصان إلا الإثم. ولو ترك الصلاة في أيام التشريق فقضاها في غير أيام التشريق لا يكبّر ؛ لأنه ليس له التكبير بالجهر شرعا، وقلنا في التكبير في أيام التشريق إنما هو الماثور عن خليل الله الجهر فيها وقد مضت فسقط.
(۱) قوله : [ إن أمكن... إلخ ] أي لَمّا كان هذا أداء من وجه دون وجه كان له جهتان أيضاً من اعتبــار الوجود وعدم اعتباره، فإن كان له مثل ينجبر به أداء نقصانه يجبر به ويجبر المؤدّي على تسليمه أي: تسليم مثل النقصان، سواء كان المثل معقولاً صورةً ومعنى أو معنى فقط، أو غير معقول لكنّه اعتبره الشارع جابراً له كسجدة السهو أو الدماء في جنايات الحجّ، ولو لم يكن له جابر سقط حقه في الأداء ويعتبر الامتثال والأداء موجودا، كذا في "الحصول".
(۲) قوله: [إذ لا مثل له... إلخ لأنه إما أن يقضي الوصف وحده وهو باطل؛ لأنه لا يعقل له مثــــل ولا يوجد نص له، أو مع الأصل بأن يقضي الصلاة معدلة الأركان أو يقضي نفس الركن بصفة الاعتدال باطل لما فيه إبطال الأصل بواسطة بطلان الوصف وهو نقض الأصول وقلب المعقول.
أيضاً وهو (۳) قوله: [فسقط] لأنّ إيجاب المثل إمّا بالعقل بأن يدرك بالعقل له مثل ليتمكن الإيجاب بالسبب الموجب للأداء، وإما بالسمع بأن جعل الشرع له مثلاً، فإذا لم يوجد واحد منهما يسقط، والاعتدال في الأركان وصف ليس له منفرداً عن الأصل مثل لا عقلاً ولا شرعاً، فلا يضمن بشيء سوى الإثم، كذا في "الفصول".
(٤) قوله: [في غير أيام ... إلخ قيّد به؛ لأنه إذا قضاها في هذه الأيام من هذه السنة بجماعة فإنّه ] يكبر؛ لأنّ وقت التكبير قائم وهو أيام التشريق، وقال الشافعي رحمه الله في أصل المسألة: مع التكبير ليكون علي نسب الفوات، ونحن نقول : الجهر بالتكبير بدعة إلا في زمـــان مخصوص، كذا قيل.
(5) قوله: [وقلنا... إلخ] هذا أيضاً تفريع على الأصل المذكور وهو أنه إن أمكن جبر النقصان بالمثل ينجبر به وإلا يسقط، لكن المسائل المتقدّمة متفرعة على الشطر الثاني أي: وإن لم يكن جبره المسائل على الشطر الأوّل أي أنه إذا أمكن جبر النقصان بالمثل ففي الواجبات جعل الشرع سجدة السهو لينجبر النقصان اللازم بترك الواجب من واجبات الصلاة كذا في "الفصول".
فصل الواجب بحكم الأمر نوعان
ترك قراءة الفاتحة والقنوت والتشهد وتكبيرات العيدين: إنه ينجبر بالسهو أي النقصان. ولو طاف طواف الفرض محدثا ينجبر ذلك بالدم وهو مثل له شرعا، وعلى هذا لو أدّى زيّفا مكان جيد فهلك عند القابض لا شيء له على المديون عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله لانه لا مثل لصفة الجودة منفردة حتى يمكن جبرها بالمثل، ولو سلم العبد مباح الدم بجناية عند الغاصب أو عند البائع بعد البيع قبل التسليم إلى المشتري.
(۱) قوله: [الفاتحة] اعلم أنّ أقسام القرآن ثمانية : الأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد والقصص والأمثال والناسخ والمنسوخ، وهذه السورة مشتملة على ذلك، فإن قوله: ﴿ الْحَمْدُ لله يشير إلى الأمر بحمده والنهي عن ضده، وقوله: ﴿رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ قصص عن إيجاد الخلائق أجمعين، وقوله: مَالِكِ يَوْمِ الدِّينِ فيه وعد ﴿ ووعيد، وقوله: الصِّرَاطَ المُستَقِيمَ أمثال، وأنعَمتَ عَلَيهِمْ هذه شريعتهم ناسخة، وقوله: ﴿غَيرِ المَغضُوبِ عَلَيهِمْ وَلَا الضَّالِّينَ ﴾ أي : اليهود والنصارى من شريعتهم منسوخة.
(۲) قوله: [فهلك... إلخ] إنما قيد به؛ لأنه إذا كان قائماً في يد ربّ الدين و لم يكن عالماً القبض كان له أن يفسخ الأداء ويطالب بالجياد إحياء لحقه في الوصف.
(۳) قوله عند أبي حنيفة] إنّما قال هذا؛ لأنه هو العامل بالقياس وقد قوي باطن هذه القياس فيكــون راجحاً على الاستحسان، أما أبو يوسف رحمه الله تعالى فعمل بالاستحسان وهو أنه يضمن مثل مــــا قبض إحياء لحقه في الجودة؛ لأنّ حقه مراعى في الوصف كما في القدر فيردّ مثل المقبوض ويستوفي الجياد.
(٤) قوله: [منفردةً لا صورةً ولا معنى أمّا صورةً فلأنها عرض يستحيل قيامها بذاتها فلا يمكن فصل العرض عن العين، وأمّا معنى فلأنّ الجودة لا قيمة لها في الأموال الربوية لقوله عليه السلام: «جَيِّدُهَا وَرَدِيتُهَـــا سَوَاء» الحديث.
(٥) قوله: [بجناية] إيراد هذه المسألة وما بعدها في هذا المقام مشكل؛ لأنه عطف ظاهراً على المسائل المتفرّعة على الأصل المذكور وهو أنه إن أمكن جبر النقصان بالمثل ينجبر به وإلا يسقط، وليس في هذه المسائل جبر النقصان بالمثل ولا سقوط بل هاهنا أمر ثالث وهو وجوب الضمان بالمثل، كذا في "الفصول".
Section: The obligatory by virtue of command is of two types. If it is possible to compensate the deficiency by its like, it is compensated by it; otherwise, the ruling of deficiency is dropped except for sin. And based on this, if one leaves the adjustment of the pillars in the matter of prayer, it cannot be made up by its like, rationally or legally. Because there is no like for it with the servant, so the ruling of deficiency is dropped except for sin. And if one leaves prayer during the days of Tashriq and then makes it up on other days, he does not say the takbir, because there is no legal basis for saying it loudly. And we have said that the takbir during the days of Tashriq is a tradition from the Friend of Allah (Ibrahim) to say it loudly, and those days have passed, so it is dropped. (1) He said: ['If it is possible... etc.'] means that since this is a performance from one aspect and not from another, it has two aspects regarding consideration of existence and non-existence. If it has a like that compensates for the deficiency in performance, it is compensated by it, and the performer is compelled to deliver it, i.e., deliver the like of the deficiency, whether the like is reasonable in form and meaning, or in meaning only, or not reasonable but the Lawgiver has considered it compensatory, like the prostration of forgetfulness or blood offerings for Hajj violations. And if there is no compensatory, his right to performance is dropped, and compliance and performance are considered existing, as in al-Husul. (2) He said: [Because there is no like for it... etc.] because either he performs the attribute alone, which is invalid because no like is conceivable for it and no text exists for it, or with the original, such as performing the prayer with adjusted pillars, or performing the pillar itself with the attribute of moderation, which is invalid because it involves invalidating the original through the invalidity of the attribute, which overturns principles and reverses reason. Also (3) He said: [It is dropped] because the obligation of the like is either by reason, i.e., reason perceives a like for it to enable obligation by the cause that necessitates performance, or by revelation, i.e., the Law has made a like for it. If neither exists, it is dropped. And moderation in the pillars is an attribute that has no like independent of the original, neither rationally nor legally, so nothing is guaranteed except sin, as in al-Fusul. (4) He said: [On other days... etc.] He restricted it with this because if he makes it up during those days of this year in congregation, he does say the takbir, because the time for takbir is present, i.e., the days of Tashriq. Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said in the original issue: He does the takbir so that the relationship of neglect is traced. And we say: Loud takbir is an innovation except in a specific time, as it is said. (5) He said: [And we said... etc.] This is also a branch of the aforementioned principle: if it is possible to compensate the deficiency by its like, it is compensated; otherwise, it is dropped. But the preceding issues are branched from the second part, i.e., if there is no compensation. The issues here are on the first part, i.e., if it is possible to compensate the deficiency by its like, then in obligatory acts, the Law has made the prostration of forgetfulness to compensate the deficiency resulting from leaving a wajib of the prayer, as in al-Fusul. Section: The obligatory by virtue of command is of two types. Leaving the recitation of al-Fatiha, al-Qunut, al-Tashahhud, and the takbirs of the two Eids: it is compensated by forgetfulness, i.e., the deficiency. And if one performs the obligatory Tawaf while in a state of hadath (impurity), that is compensated by a blood offering, which is its like legally. And based on this, if one pays a false coin instead of a good one and it perishes in the hands of the receiver, the debtor owes nothing according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, because the attribute of excellence has no separate like that can compensate for it. And if a slave who is licit to be killed due to a crime is handed over to the usurper or to the seller after the sale but before delivery to the buyer, (1) He said: [al-Fatiha] Know that the divisions of the Quran are eight: command, prohibition, promise, threat, stories, parables, abrogating and abrogated. This Surah contains them all. For His saying: 'Praise be to Allah' indicates the command to praise Him and the prohibition of its opposite. His saying: 'Lord of the Worlds' is a story about the creation of all creatures. His saying: 'Master of the Day of Judgment' contains promise and threat. His saying: 'The straight path' is a parable. 'Those upon whom You have bestowed favor' is their Shariah which abrogates. His saying: 'Not of those who have earned Your anger nor of those who go astray' means the Jews and Christians, from their Shariah which is abrogated. (2) He said: [it perishes... etc.] He restricted it with this because if it remains in the hands of the creditor and he was not aware of its defect, he has the option to rescind the payment and demand good coins to revive his right to the attribute. (3) He said: [According to Abu Hanifa] He only said this because he is the one who acts by analogy, and the hidden aspect of this analogy is strong, so it is preponderant over istihsan. As for Abu Yusuf, may Allah the Exalted have mercy on him, he acted by istihsan: that he guarantees a like of what he received to revive his right to the attribute of excellence, because his right is observed in the attribute just as it is in quantity; so he returns the equivalent of what was received and collects the good coins. (4) He said: [Separately, neither in form nor in meaning] As for form, because it is an accident that cannot subsist by itself, so it is impossible to separate the accident from the substance. As for meaning, because excellence has no value in usurious wealth due to his, peace be upon him, saying: 'Its good and its bad are equal' - the hadith. (5) He said: [Due to a crime] The introduction of this issue and what follows in this context is problematic because it is apparently connected to the issues branched from the mentioned principle, i.e., if possible, compensate; if not, drop. But in these issues there is neither compensation by a like nor dropping; rather, there is a third matter: the obligation of guarantee by a like, as in al-Fusul.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Usul al-Shashi explains a key Hanafi legal principle: when an obligatory act (wajib) has a deficiency that can be compensated by something similar (mithl), the deficiency is remedied; otherwise, the legal effect of the deficiency is dropped, but the sin remains. The commentator elaborates with multiple examples. The first example is the adjustment of pillars (ta'dil al-arkan) in prayer—this cannot be made up by a like, so the deficiency is dropped but sin remains. The second example is making up a missed prayer from the days of Tashriq on other days; the takbir is not repeated because the time for its like has passed. The third set of examples involves wajibs that have compensatory acts: leaving qira'at al-Fatiha, qunut, tashahhud, and takbirs of the two Eids are compensated by the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw). Performing tawaf while in a state of hadath is compensated by a blood offering (dam). The commentator also discusses the case of paying a false coin instead of a good one. According to Abu Hanifa, if the false coin is lost, the debtor owes nothing because the attribute of excellence has no independent like that can be compensated separately. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) disagree, using istihsan to argue that the debtor must compensate with a like of the coin because the creditor's right to the attribute of quality is preserved. The passage also includes a tangential note on Surah al-Fatiha containing all eight types of Quranic content, and a concluding note questioning why certain cases (like the slave) are included in this discussion, as they involve a third scenario—obligation of guarantee by like—rather than compensation or dropping.

Key Terms
الواجب بحكم الأمر (al-wajib bi hukm al-amr): An obligatory act that becomes wajib by virtue of a direct command (amr) from the Lawgiver.
المثل (al-mithl): A like or equivalent that can compensate for a deficiency in an act, either in form, meaning, or by legal designation.
جبر النقصان (jabr al-nuqsan): Compensating for a deficiency in a wajib act by performing its like (mithl) or by an act deemed compensatory by the Lawgiver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on leaving the recitation of Surah al-Fatiha in prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The deficiency is compensated by the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw).
C) The deficiency is dropped but the person is sinful.
D) The person must make up the prayer with takbir.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle of jabr al-nuqsan distinguishes between wajib deficiencies that have a legal like (compensated) and those that do not (dropped, but sin remains), balancing obligation and practicality.

The Precedence of Actual Performance over Substitution
Establishes the usul principle of performance precedence over substitution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that actual performance (ada) takes precedence over substitution (qada) to identify the correct ruling in cases of defective delivery and usurpation.

Core Idea
Performance (ada) is the default; substitution (qada) is only permitted when performance is impossible.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi establishes a foundational principle of Hanafi legal theory: the priority of actual performance over substitution. The author applies this principle to three concrete fiqh scenarios—deposit, usurpation, and sales with defects—to illustrate how the rule governs practical rulings. Understanding this principle helps you trace how Usul al-Fiqh rules map onto Fiqh branches.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
State the maxim that performance (ada) takes precedence over substitution (qada).
2
Analyze the definition of ada
Break down the legal definition of ada: it is the original obligated act, whether complete or incomplete.
3
Apply to deposit, agency, and usurpation
Explain why the depositor/agent/usurper cannot keep the item and pay its value.
4
Apply to defective sale
Understand why the buyer's option is limited to keeping or returning, not demanding price reduction.
5
Compare the Shafi'i counter-argument on drastic change
Note the disagreement on when performance is considered impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الأصل في هذا الباب هو الأداء كاملا كان أو ناقصا لأنه خلف عنه والخلف لا يعتبر إلا عند تعذر الأصل. وإنما يصار إلى القضاء عند تعذر الأداء، ولهذا يتعين المال في الوديعة والوكالة والغصب ولو أراد المودع والوكيل والغاصب أن يمسك العين ويدفع ما يماثله ليس له ذلك. ولو باع شيئا وسلمه فظهر به عيب كان المشتري بالخيار بين الأخذ والترك فيه وباعتبار أن الأصل هو الأداء يقول لأن الأداء لم يتعذر وهو تسليمه سليما لأنه مبنى العقد عليه. لأنه الأداء ولو قاصرا فيقدم على القضاء وهو دفع القيمة. الشافعي: الواجب على الغاصب رد العين المغصوبة وإن تغيرت في يد الغاصب تغيرا فاحشا ويجب الأرش بسبب النقصان.
Then the fundamental principle in this chapter is actual performance, whether complete or incomplete, because it is the substitute for it, and the substitute is only considered when the original is impossible. And substitution is only resorted to when actual performance is impossible. For this reason, property is specifically identified in deposit, agency, and usurpation: if the depositor, agent, or usurper wishes to retain the specific item and pay its equivalent, they are not allowed. And if someone sold something and delivered it, and a defect then appeared, the purchaser has the option between retaining and returning it. And considering that the principle is actual performance, he says: because performance is not impossible, and it is delivery soundly because the contract is built upon it. Because it is performance, even if deficient, it takes precedence over substitution, which is paying the value. Al-Shafi'i says: The obligation upon the usurper is to return the usurped property even if it has changed in his hand drastically, and the compensation for the deficiency is obligatory, i.e., guarantee of the deficiency.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage establishes a key usul al-fiqh principle: in matters of performance (ada) and substitution (qada), the original act of performance takes precedence. The commentary expands on the matn statement 'the principle in this chapter is performance, whether complete or incomplete.' Performance is considered the original duty; substitution is only resorted to when performance is impossible. This principle is applied to various fiqh issues. First, in deposit, agency, and usurpation, the specific item (like gold coins) is tied to its identity; the depositor, agent, or usurper cannot simply pay its equivalent but must return the actual item. Second, in sale with a defect, since the seller delivered the item (performance has occurred, albeit deficient), the buyer has the choice to accept the defective item or return it, but cannot demand a reduction in price—because paying the difference would be substitution (qada), which is not allowed when performance (even deficient) is possible. The passage also records the Shafi'i position: a usurper must return the property even if it has changed drastically, and must compensate for the deficiency. The Hanafi position differs on when ownership transfers. The principle is rational (talil) and derived from the nature of obligations: the original duty (ada) is the intended act, and qada is only a backup.

Key Terms
الأداء (al-adā'): Actual performance or delivery of the specific item owed, whether complete or incomplete.
القضاء (al-qaḍā'): Substitute performance, such as paying the value or compensation, when original performance is impossible.
الخلف (al-khalaf): Substitute; here it refers to qada as a replacement for the original ada.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle stated in the passage, if a buyer receives a defective item, what are his options?
A) He may keep the item and demand a reduction in price.
B) He may only return the item or keep it as is.
C) He may keep the item and sue for damages.
D) He must return the item and demand a full refund.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle that actual performance (ada) takes precedence over substitution (qada) governs rulings in deposit, usurpation, and defective sales: performance must be rendered if possible, even if incomplete, before substitution is permitted.

Kamil and Qasir Compensation in Ghasp: The Timing Dispute
Matn and hashya on types of compensation and internal dispute on valuation timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two types of compensation (kamil and qasir) in Ghasp, identify the dispute among the three Hanafi imams on the valuation date of a lost fungible, and apply the Hanafi rule that compensation defaults to a perfect substitute.

Core Idea
Compensation defaults to a perfect substitute; only when impossible does value substitute, and valuation date is disputed among the founders.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi doctrine of compensation for usurped property. The matn distinguishes between complete compensation (delivery of a fungible substitute) and deficient compensation (value). The hashya expands on the internal Hanafi disagreement regarding when to assess the value of a fungible that has become unavailable—on the day of litigation, usurpation, or unavailability. Understanding this dispute reveals how the school weighs competing principles: the moment of liability versus the moment of impossibility. Additionally, the passage explains that usufructs (manafi‘) are not compensable because they lack a measurable financial equivalent, a distinct Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of compensation
From the matn: 'compensation is of two types: complete and deficient.' Complete is delivery of a perfect substitute (mithl) matching in form and meaning, e.g., a bushel of wheat for a bushel of wheat. Deficient is delivery of value (qima) when a perfect substitute is impossible, e.g., a sheep that perished—value is paid because no exact same sheep can be guaranteed.
2
Understand the default principle
The matn states: 'The principle is complete compensation.' Recourse to deficient is only when the complete is impossible. This establishes a hierarchical rule: first attempt mithl, then fallback to qima.
3
Analyze the internal dispute on valuation date
For a lost fungible, Abu Hanifa says value on the day of litigation, because inability to deliver the substitute only becomes clear at litigation. Abu Yusuf says value on the day of usurpation, because that is when the obligation (daman) arose. Muhammad says value on the day the item becomes unavailable among people, because inability is realized then.
The dispute hinges on the illa (cause) for resorting to value: is it the obligation itself, the factual unavailability, or the judicial determination?
4
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The matn says 'upon this Abu Hanifa said...' and the commentary does not override. The phrase 'ala hadha qal implies reliance on Abu Hanifa's view for fatwa. The hashya presents the other views but does not reject them.
In later Hanafi works, Abu Hanifa's view is usually taken as mufta bihi.
5
Apply the principle to usufructs
The text concludes that usufructs (e.g., riding a usurped animal, using a house) are not compensable by mithl or qima because they have no substitute in form or meaning. They are only sinful but not financially liable. This is a key Hanafi ikhtilaf with other schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قوله: [ضمن قيمتها أي قيمة الشاة؛ لأن حق المستحق في الصورة والمعنى جميعا إلا أن حقه في الصورة قد فات للعجز عن القضاء، فبقي حقه في المعنى وهي القيمة.
قوله: [والقيمة...] لأنها تعادل الشاة في المالية وتقوم مقامها ولذا سميت قيمة.
قوله: [الكامل] أي: الأداء بالمثل صورة ومعنى، فإن فيه رعاية حق المستحق صورة ومعنى.
قوله: [قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله ...] وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله: يضمن قيمته يوم الغصب؛ لأنه هو الموجب للضمان لا الخصومة، فاعتبار قيمة المضمون وقت تحقق الضمان أولى من اعتباره وقت الخصومة، وقال محمد رحمه الله: يضمن قيمته يوم الانقطاع عن أيدي الناس؛ لأن الواجب هو المثل وإنما يصار إلى القيمة للعجز عنه، والعجز إنما يتحقق عند الانقطاع عن أيدي الناس، كذا في "المعدن".
قوله: [لا يمكن إيجاب القضاء فيه بالمثل] يعني: إنما وجب الضمان بالمثل الكامل أو بالقاصر فيما له مثل أو له قيمة، وأما ما لا قيمة له فلا يضمن إلا بالإثم؛ لأنه لا مثل له صورة ولا معنى إلا أن يرد الشرع بالمثل له صورة كما ذكر بعد هذه المسائل، كذا في "الفصول".
قوله: [ولهذا المعنى] أي: لأجل أن ما لا مثل له لا صورة ولا معنى لا يمكن إيجاب القضاء فيه، كذا "الفصول".
قوله: [لا تضمن بالإتلاف وصورة إتلاف المنافع أن يستعمل الأعيان المغصوبة بأن يستخدم العبد أو يركب الدابة المغصوبة ويسكن البيت فإنه لا يجب ضمانها على المتلف لا بمثلها ولا بقيمتها؛ لأن
And as for compensation, it is of two types: complete and deficient. The complete is delivery of a substitute for the obligatory in form and meaning, like one who usurped a bushel of wheat and consumed it, he guarantees a bushel of wheat and the delivered becomes a similar for the first in form and meaning, and similarly the ruling in all fungible items. As for the deficient, it is delivery of what does not resemble the obligatory in form but resembles in meaning, like one who usurped a sheep and it perished, he guarantees its value, and the value is similar to the sheep in meaning not in form, and recourse to the deficient is only when the complete is impossible. The principle is complete compensation, and upon this Abu Hanifa said: if one usurps a fungible and it perishes in his hand and it becomes unavailable among people, he guarantees its value on the day of litigation because inability to deliver the complete substitute only appears at litigation. Before litigation, it is not because the possibility of obtaining a perfect substitute is conceivable. As for what has no substitute in form or meaning, it is not possible to impose compensation by substitute, and for this reason we said that usufructs are not guaranteed by destruction because imposing guarantee for destruction is neither by their substitute nor by their value. His saying: [he guarantees its value, i.e., the value of the sheep] because the right of the claimant is in both form and meaning, but his right in form is lost due to inability to compensate, so his right in meaning remains, which is the value. His saying: [and the value...] because it equals the sheep in financial value and stands in its place, hence it is called value. His saying: [the complete] i.e., delivery by substitute in form and meaning, for in it is observance of the claimant's right in form and meaning. His saying: [Abu Hanifa said...] Abu Yusuf said: he guarantees its value on the day of usurpation because it is the one that necessitates guarantee, not litigation, so considering the value at the time guarantee is established is more appropriate than considering it at the time of litigation. Muhammad said: he guarantees its value on the day of unavailability among people because the obligatory is the substitute, and one resorts to value only due to inability, and inability is only realized at the time of unavailability among people, as in al-Ma'dan. His saying: [it is not possible to impose compensation by substitute] means: guarantee is imposed by the complete substitute or by the deficient only for what has a substitute or value. As for what has no value, it is not guaranteed except by sin because it has no substitute in form or meaning, unless the Law brings a substitute in form as mentioned after these cases, as in al-Fusul. His saying: [and for this meaning] i.e., because what has no substitute in form or meaning cannot have compensation imposed in it, as in al-Fusul. His saying: [it is not guaranteed by destruction, and the form of destroying usufructs is using the usurped property, like employing a slave, riding a usurped animal, or living in a house. Then no guarantee is obligatory upon the destroyer, neither by their substitute nor by their value, because...
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage from the hashya (with the matn base) explains the two types of compensation in cases of usurpation (ghasp). The matn states that the default is compensation with a perfect substitute (mithl) that matches in both form and essence, which is possible for fungible items (mithliyyat) like wheat. When that is impossible, the deficient substitute (qasir) is used, which is monetary value (qima) that matches only in meaning/essence, not form (e.g., sheep value). The hashya deepens by analyzing that the right of the claimant encompasses both form and meaning; when form is lost due to inability to deliver the exact item, the right in meaning (value) remains. The passage then records a key ikhtilaf among the three founders: Abu Hanifa holds that the time for valuing a fungible that has become unavailable is the day of litigation, because inability to deliver is only known then; Abu Yusuf says the day of usurpation (since that is when the liability began); Muhammad says the day the item becomes unavailable from the market. This disagreement affects the amount of compensation. The commentary also clarifies that usufructs (manafi') like riding or using a house are not compensable because they have no substitute or value—they are not 'ayn, so the principle of 'guarantee' does not apply in the same way. The cause (illa) is that they lack a measurable financial equivalent. This is a distinctive Hanafi position; Shafi'i school may differ.

Key Terms
القضاء الكامل (al-qada' al-kamil): Compensation with a perfect substitute matching in form and meaning.
المثليات (al-mithliyyat): Fungible items like weighed, measured, or countable goods.
القضاء القاصر (al-qada' al-qasir): Deficient compensation by paying value (qima) when perfect substitute is impossible.
المنافع (al-manafi'): Usufructs; benefits derived from property (e.g., riding, using).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when is the value of a lost fungible determined?
A) Day of usurpation
B) Day of litigation
C) Day of unavailability
D) Day of market price change

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, compensation defaults to a perfect substitute; only when that is impossible does value substitute, and Abu Hanifa's valuation at litigation day is the relied-upon position.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Benefits in Usurpation: Hanafi Non-Guarantee and the Shafi'i Rebuttal
Usul dispute: non-guarantee of benefits in usurpation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi ruling on guarantee of benefits (manafi') in usurpation (ghasb), state the three proofs, and explain why the Shafi'i analogy to hire is rejected using istihsan.

Core Idea
Benefits are non-permanent accidents, thus not guaranteed in usurpation; hire is an exception by necessity, not analogy.

This passage addresses a foundational dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i over whether the benefits (manafi') of a usurped object must be compensated. The Hanafi position is that benefits are not guaranteed because they are accidents (a'rad) that cannot be captured or valued like substances. The Shafi'i school argues that since benefits are valuable in hire contracts, they should also be guaranteed in usurpation. The text provides three Hanafi proofs and responds to the Shafi'i argument, distinguishing between qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Dispute
State the Hanafi ruling: benefits of a usurped object are not guaranteed. Contrast with the Shafi'i view that they are guaranteed. Recognize that the issue is whether benefits are legally valuable property.
The practical difference: a usurper of a slave must pay for the slave's service in Shafi'i but not in Hanafi.
2
Examine the Three Hanafi Proofs
Study the text's three arguments: (1) Benefits are accidents (a'rad) that do not remain, so they cannot be taken from the owner; (2) Usurpation requires a permanent object, which benefits lack; (3) Guarantee requires similitude (mumathala), and benefits cannot resemble substances due to their fleeting nature and variation.
Each proof reinforces the idea that benefits lack the necessary characteristics for guarantee.
3
Understand the Shafi'i Counter-Argument
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that benefits are legally valuable (mutaqawwim) as proven by the validity of hire (ijarah) contracts, where benefits are exchanged for rent. Therefore, by analogy (qiyas), they should be guaranteed in usurpation.
The Shafi'i rely on the existence of a market value for benefits.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response: Istihsan vs. Qiyas
The Hanafi response rejects the analogy: hire is permitted by istihsan (juristic preference) to fulfill human needs, not by qiyas on the nature of benefits. The ruling for hire does not extend to usurpation because what is established by necessity does not go beyond its place.
This is a classic use of istihsan to override qiyas in Hanafi usul.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi would not impose any monetary liability for the use of a usurped object, while a Shafi'i would require compensation equivalent to the rental value. The sin of usurpation remains, but compensation is deferred to the Hereafter.
This shows how a difference in usul leads to different fatwas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل الواجب بحكم الأمر نوعان
لأنها عرض و العين جوهر.
بالمثل متعذر وإيجابه بالعين كذلك ؛ لأن العين لا تماثل المنفعة لا صورة ولا معنى كما إذا غصب عبدا فاستخدمه شهرا أو دارا فسكن فيها شهرا ثم رد أي الدار أو العبد أي الدار. فإنه يقول بضمان المنافع قياسا على تقومها في الإجارة. المغصوب إلى المالك لا يجب عليه ضمان المنافع خلافاً للشافعي، فبقي الإثم حكما له وانتقل جزاؤه إلى دار الآخرة، ولهذا المعنى قلنا: لا تضمن منافع أي الغصب والإتلاف. إيجاب الضمان بمثلها من المنافع متعذر ؛ لأنّ المنافع تتفاوت تفاوتاً كثيراً على حسب تفاوت أعيانها، فإنّ منفعة عبد مثلاً لا تماثل منفعة عبد آخر للتفاوت بين المنفعتين، كذا في بعض شروح "المنار".
(1) قوله: [متعذر] لأنّ المنافع تتفاوت تفاوتاً كثيراً على حسب تفاوت أعيانها، فإنّ منفعة عبد مثلاً لا يماثل منفعة عبد آخر للتفاوت بين المنفعتين كذا في "المعدن".
(2) قوله: [لأنّ العين لا تماثل المنفعة ... آه] أما صورةً فظاهر، وأما معنى فلأن المنافع أعراض لا تبقى زمانين فلا يمكن إحرازها، وما لا يمكن إحرازها لا يمكن تقويمها وما لا يتقوّم لا يمكن فيه إيجاب الضمان بالقيمة، والمثل المعنوي هو القيمة، كذا قالوا وفيه اشتباه وهو أنّ الإجارة إنما شرعت في الشرع على تقويم المنافع، وقيتمها تصير معلومةً بتقديرها بالأزمنة وبأنفسها أيضاً عند التجارة، فكيف يصح أن يقال: «إنّ العين لا تماثل المنفعة»، كذا في "الفصول" وأجيب عنه: أنّ القياس يمنع الإجارة لاستحالة إحراز المنافع حقيقةً لعدم بقاءها إلا أنا جوّزناها استحساناً بناءً على قيام العين مقام المنفعة بطريق الخلافة دفعاً للضرورة وقضاءً للحوائج، فإنّ من احتاج إلى سكنى الدار وخدمة العبد وركوب الدابة ولا يمكن أن يشتري فلا بدّ من الاستيجار والثابت بالضرورة لا يتعدّى عن محلها، كذا في "المعدن".
(3) قوله: [خلافاً للشافعي رحمه الله] فإنّ عنده يجب عليه ضمان المنافع؛ لأنها متقومة شرعاً كما في الإجارة، ولنا وجوه الأوّل : أنها أعراض فلا تبقى فحصلت على ملك الغاصب لحدوثها في مكانه فيملكها؛ إذ لم تحدث في يد المالك، والثاني: سبب الضمان هو الغصب والمنافع لا تصلح أن تكون مغصوبة ومتلفة؛ لأنها لا بقاء لها وما لا يبقى لا يتصوّر غصبه وإتلافه؛ إذ موردهما البقاء فلا تضمن، والثالث : أنّ الضمان مشروط بالمماثلة وهي لا تماثل الأعيان لسرعة فنائها وبقاء الأعيان فلا تماثل المنافع للاختلاف الفاحش في المنتفع والمنتفع به، وأمّا تقوّمها بعقد الإجارة فللضرورة فلا يعدّدها فاحفظه، ولا تكن من الغافلين كذا في "الحصول".
Chapter: The obligatory by command is of two types. Because it is an accident and the substance is a substance. The like is impossible, and making it obligatory with the substance is likewise; because the substance does not resemble the benefit neither in form nor meaning, as when one usurps a slave and uses him for a month, or a house and lives in it for a month, then returns the house or the slave. So he says that benefits are guaranteed by analogy to their valuation in hire. It is not obligatory on the usurper to guarantee the benefits, contrary to al-Shafi'i, so the sin remains as a ruling for him and its recompense transfers to the abode of the Hereafter; and for this meaning we say: Benefits of usurpation and destruction are not guaranteed. Making the guarantee with their like from benefits is impossible; because benefits vary greatly according to the variation of their substances, for the benefit of, for example, one slave does not resemble the benefit of another slave due to the difference between the two benefits, as in some commentaries of al-Manar. (1) His saying: [impossible] because benefits vary greatly according to the variation of their substances, so the benefit of one slave does not resemble the benefit of another slave due to the difference between the two benefits, as in al-Ma'dan. (2) His saying: [because the substance does not resemble the benefit...] As for form, it is apparent; as for meaning, because benefits are accidents that do not remain two moments, so they cannot be captured, and what cannot be captured cannot be valued, and what is not valuable cannot have guarantee imposed by value, and the figurative like is value. They said so, and there is confusion: that hire was legislated in the Shariah on the valuation of benefits, and their value becomes known by estimating them with times and also by themselves in trade; so how is it correct to say: 'The substance does not resemble the benefit'? As in al-Fusul. And it is answered: that analogy prevents hire due to the impossibility of actually capturing benefits because they do not remain, except that we permitted it by istihsan based on the substance taking the place of the benefit by way of substitution to remove necessity and fulfill needs. So whoever needs to live in a house, use a slave, or ride an animal, and cannot buy, must hire. What is established by necessity does not extend beyond its place, as in al-Ma'dan. (3) His saying: [Contrary to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him] For him, guarantee of benefits is obligatory because they are legally valuable as in hire. For us are proofs: First, they are accidents, so they do not remain, so they come into the possession of the usurper because they occur in his place, so he owns them, since they did not occur in the hand of the owner. Second, the cause of guarantee is usurpation and benefits are not suitable to be usurped or destroyed because they have no permanence; what does not remain cannot be conceived as usurped or destroyed; since their subject requires permanence, so they are not guaranteed. Third, guarantee is conditional on similitude, and they do not resemble substances due to their quick perishing and the permanence of substances; thus benefits do not resemble substances due to the gross difference in the benefit and the thing benefited from. As for their valuation by hire contract, it is for necessity, so do not extend it. So memorize this and do not be among the heedless, as in al-Husul.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the guarantee of benefits (manafi') in cases of usurpation (ghasb). The author begins by stating that benefits are accidents (a'rad) while substances (a'yan) are substances (jawhar). Since benefits are perishable and do not last, they cannot be taken as property in the same way substances are. The Hanafi position is that if someone usurps an object like a slave or house and uses it for a month, upon returning it, he is not required to compensate for the benefits used, contrary to al-Shafi'i. The rationale is that benefits have no material existence that can be guaranteed; they are generated by the user and are not taken from the owner. The author provides several proofs: first, benefits are accidents that do not remain, so they cannot be the subject of guarantee; second, the cause of guarantee (ghasb) requires permanence, which benefits lack; third, guarantee requires similitude (mumathala), but benefits cannot be compared to substances because they are ephemeral and vary greatly. The counter-argument that benefits are valued in hire contracts is addressed by distinguishing that hire is permitted by istihsan (juristic preference) out of necessity, not by qiyas (analogy). Therefore, the ruling for hire does not apply to usurpation. The Shafi'i position that benefits are legally valuable like in hire is thus rejected. The author concludes that the sin remains but the compensation is deferred to the afterlife. This is a classic Hanafi usul argument relying on the nature of benefits as non-permanent accidents.

Key Terms
المنافع (al-manāfiʿ): Benefits or usufruct derived from a substance, considered accidents (a'rad) in Hanafi jurisprudence.
الغصب (al-ghaṣb): Wrongful appropriation of another's property without right, a cause for guarantee of the substance but not necessarily benefits.
الضمان (al-ḍamān): Legal liability to compensate for loss or damage, conditional on similitude (mumathala) in Hanafi thought.
الإجارة (al-ijārah): Hire contract; a transaction where the benefit of an object is exchanged for rent, considered an exception (istihsan) in Hanafi usul for this discussion.
الاستحسان (al-istihsān): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that permits an exception to an analogy due to necessity, custom, or other considerations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone usurps a house and lives in it for a month, upon returning the house, he must:
A) Pay rent equal to the market value for the month.
B) Not pay anything for the use.
C) Pay half the rental value as compensation.
D) Pay only if the owner explicitly requests it.

Key Takeaway
Benefits are not guaranteed in usurpation because they are accidents; hire is an exception by necessity (istihsan), not a basis for analogy.

The Particle 'Aw' Meaning 'Until' in Oaths
Establishing that 'aw' can mean 'hatta' in oaths and legal contexts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when 'aw' functions as 'hatta' in oaths and legal texts, apply the Hanafi contextual principle to derive rulings, and analyze the Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
In oaths, 'aw' means 'until' when the two clauses are incompatible.

This lesson examines the exceptional use of the Arabic particle 'aw' (or) to mean 'until' (hatta) in legal language, particularly in oaths. By analyzing a Quranic verse and Hanafi examples, you will learn how context determines meaning and how this affects legal rulings on oath-breaking.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic phenomenon
Recognize that the particle 'aw' in certain contexts does not indicate choice or doubt but rather a future condition, effectively meaning 'until'.
This is an exceptional meaning, not the default.
2
Analyze the Quranic evidence
Examine Aal-E-Imran 3:128 where 'aw' links a negative statement to a future event. Determine why the meaning 'or' is impossible and 'until' is necessary.
The verse is the basis for the principle.
3
Extract the effective cause (illah)
Identify that the incompatibility of the two clauses (one negative, one positive) prevents simple conjunction, forcing 'aw' to mean 'until'.
This illah is what allows qiyas to oath statements.
4
Apply qiyas jali to oaths
Transfer the ruling from the Quranic example to oath statements like 'I will not enter this house or I enter that house.' The illah of incompatibility is present.
The Hanafi school relies on this analogy.
5
Derive the fiqh ruling
Conclude that the oath is broken only if the condition (the second act) does not occur first. For example, if he enters the first house before the second, he breaks the oath.
The ruling follows from the meaning of 'hatta'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يكون «أو» بمعنى حتى. قال الله تعالى: لَيْسَ لَكَ مِنَ الْأَمْرِ شَيْءٌ أَوْ يَتُوبَ عَلَيْهِمْ [آل عمران: ۱۲۸]. قال أصحابنا: لو قال: «لا أدخل هذه الدار أو أدخل هذه الدار» يكون «أو» بمعنى «حتى»، حتى لو دخل الأولى أولا حنث، ولو دخل الثانية أولا لا يحنث. وبمثله لو قال: «لا أفارقك أو تقضي ديني» يكون بمعنى حتى تقضي ديني.
And 'or' can be in the meaning of 'until'. Allah Almighty said: 'You have nothing of the matter, or He turns to them in mercy' [Aal-E-Imran 3:128]. Our companions said: If he says, 'I will not enter this house or I will enter this house,' then 'or' is in the meaning of 'until', such that if he enters the first one first, he breaks his oath, and if he enters the second one first, he does not break it. And similarly, if he says, 'I will not separate from you or you pay my debt,' it is in the meaning of 'until you pay my debt.'
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage deals with the exceptional use of the particle 'aw' to mean 'hatta' (until) when the two parts of the statement are incompatible. The Quranic verse (3:128) is cited as evidence: 'You have nothing of the matter, or He turns to them in mercy' — meaning 'until He turns to them.' The Hanafi scholars (as-habuna) apply this to oaths. If someone vows, 'I will not enter this house or I will enter this house,' the second part ('or I will enter...') is interpreted as a condition linked to the first. Because the two statements cannot be coordinated as alternatives, 'aw' is given the meaning of 'until.' Thus, if he enters the first house before the second, he breaks his oath (because the condition of non-entry is violated), but if he enters the second first, he does not break it because the condition is not yet fulfilled. Similarly, if he says, 'I will not separate from you until you pay my debt,' the 'aw' again means 'until.' This shows the Hanafi method of interpreting particles according to context to achieve legal coherence.

Key Terms
أو ('aw): In this context, it means 'until' (hatta) when the two parts of a sentence are mutually exclusive.
حتى (hatta): A particle meaning 'until', used to indicate a condition or limit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person swears 'لا أفارقك أو تقضي ديني' (I will not leave you until you pay my debt), when does he break his oath?
A) Immediately after swearing.
B) When he leaves the other person before the debt is paid.
C) When the debt is paid.
D) He never breaks it because the condition is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The particle 'aw' can mean 'until' when the clauses are incompatible, a principle derived from the Quran and applied by Hanafis to oaths.

Rulings Cease with Their Causes
Explaining that a ruling ends when its cause ends, with examples from zakat and purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a ruling ceases when its cause (al-‘illah) ceases, using examples from zakat and purification.

Core Idea
A ruling ends when its cause ends; this is why zakat shares for reconciliating hearts ceased after Islam's strength.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi illustrates a foundational principle in Hanafi legal theory: rulings are tied to their causes. The author provides concrete examples from zakat and purification to demonstrate that when the cause vanishes, the ruling itself ceases. Understanding this principle is essential for deriving rulings in changing circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Locate the statement: 'Sitting of the ruling due to falling of its foundation and cause.' This is the core principle that the passage will apply.
The phrase 'بناه' might be read as 'بناؤه' (foundation).
2
Examine the zakat example
The author gives the category of 'mu'allafatu qulubuhum' (those whose hearts are reconciled). Identify the cause for giving them zakat: to attract them to Islam and strengthen the community. Then note that during Abu Bakr's caliphate, when Islam was strong, the cause ceased, so the ruling (giving them zakat) ceased.
3
Examine the relatives' share example
The share of the Prophet's relatives from khums was given for support and loyalty (the cause). After the Prophet's death and the strengthening of Islam, the cause ceased, so the share ceased.
This shows the principle applied to a different context.
4
Analyze the purification example
A garment impure with physical impurity (khabath) is washed with vinegar. If the impurity disappears, the garment becomes pure because the cause (presence of impurity) is gone. This distinguishes physical impurity from ritual impurity (hadath), where the cause is not physical removal but a legal requirement for a specific purifier (water).
This example establishes the Hanafi position that vinegar purifies from khabath but not hadath.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab dispute
The author notes that al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) disagrees with this distinction. The Hanafi view is preferred because it is based on the nature of the 'illah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل إجماع هذه الأمة. أي سقوط الحكم لسقوط بناه وعلته. وباعتبار هذا المعنى سقطت المؤلفة قلوبهم عن الأصناف الثمانية لانقطاع علتهم، وسقط سهم ذوي القربى لانقطاع علته. وعلى هذا إذا غسل الثوب النجس بالخل فزالت النجاسة يحكم بطهارة المحل لانقطاع علتها وبهذا ثبت الفرق بين الحدث والخبث خلافا للشافعي رحمه الله. قوله: [سقطت ... إلخ] و ذلك لأنّ المؤلّفة قلوبهم على رسول الله صلّى الله عليه وسلّم أنهم لو تألّفوا و مالوا إلى الإسلام فمال معهم أقوام قوي أهل الإسلام، فلما أعزّ الله تعالى الإسلام والمسلمين وأغنى عنهم أي في خلافة أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه منع الزكوة عنهم لانتفاء علّتها؛ لأنّ الحكم إذا ثبت بعلة مخصوصة يرتفع بارتفاع تلك العلة. قوله: [وسقط... إلخ] أي: سقط سهم ذوي القربى وهم أقارب الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلّم لانقطاع علته، اعلم أن خمس الغنيمة يقسم على ثلثة أسهم: سهم لليتامى، وسهم للمساكين، وسبيل الله ويدخل فقراء ذوى القربى فيهم ويقدمون ولا يدفع إلى أغنيائهم وكان لذوي القربى معه لغنيهم وفقيرهم على الإطلاق، ثُمّ سقط بعد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلّم سهمهم؛ لأنه عليه السلام إنما كان يعطيهم للنصرة يدلّ عليه قوله عليه السلام: «إنهم لم يزالوا معي هكذا في الجاهلية والإسلام وشبك بين أصابعه»، فإذا أعزّ الله تعالى الإسلام وأغنى عن نصرتهم سقط سهمهم لانتفاء العلّة. قوله: [غسل الثوب النجس... آه] أي: إذا غسل الثوب النجس بالخل أو بغيره من المائعات فزالت النجاسة يحكم بطهارة المحل؛ لأنّ نجاسة المحلّ إنما يكون لعلة وجود النجاسة في المحل فإذا زالت النجاسة عن المحلّ فقد ارتفعت علته؛ وذلك لأنّ النجاسة تزول عن المحلّ حسا حقيقةً وحكماً كما تزول بالماء. قوله وبهذا] أى بأنّ علّة الطهارة زوال النجاسة ثبت الفرق بين الحدث والخبث أي: بين النجاسة الحكميّة والحقيقية حيث لا تفيد المائع طهارة الغسل والوضوء، فإنّ الخل يزيل النجس عن المحلّ، وطهارة المحلّ عن النجاسة الحقيقية بزوال النجاسة وقد وجد، وأمّا طهارة الوضوء والغسل فإنما عرفت شرعاً باستعمال المطهر وليست علتها زوال النجاسة؛ إذ لا يحس ولا يعقل نجاسة في المحلّ حتى تزول، وإنما الخلّ له أثر في زوال النجاسة لا غير، فلهذا لا يفيد طهارة الغسل والوضوء. في إزالته بغير الماء دون الحدث. أي طهارة المحل. طهارة حكمية وإن أفاد طهارة حسية حقيقية.
Section: Consensus of this Ummah. i.e., the falling away of the ruling due to the falling away of its foundation and cause. By consideration of this meaning, the [category of] those whose hearts are reconciled fell from the eight categories due to the cessation of their cause, and the share of the relatives fell due to the cessation of its cause. Based on this, if a garment that is najis (impure) is washed with vinegar and the impurity disappears, the place is ruled pure due to the cessation of its cause, and by this the difference between hadath (ritual impurity) and khabath (physical impurity) is established, contrary to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him). His saying: [they fell... etc.] That is because those whose hearts are reconciled (mu'allafa qulubuhum) – the Prophet, peace be upon him, used to give them so that they would incline to Islam and with them incline strong groups of the people of Islam, until Allah honored Islam and Muslims and made them independent of them during the caliphate of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him) and he withheld the zakat from them due to the absence of its cause; for when a ruling is established by a specific cause, it ceases with the cessation of that cause. His saying: [and the share fell... etc.] i.e., the share of the relatives (dhawu al-qurba) fell due to the cessation of its cause. Know that the khums (one-fifth) of the war booty is divided into three shares: share for orphans, share for the poor, and the way of Allah, and the poor among the relatives are included among them and given priority, and the rich among them are not given. The share for the relatives was for both their rich and poor absolutely, then after the Prophet (peace be upon him) their share fell because he, peace be upon him, used to give them for support, as indicated by his saying: 'They have been with me in this manner in Jahiliyyah and Islam' and he interlocked his fingers. So when Allah honored Islam and made them independent of their support, their share fell due to the absence of the cause. His saying: [washing the impure garment... etc.] i.e., if an impure garment is washed with vinegar or other liquids and the impurity disappears, the place is ruled pure because the impurity of the place is due to the cause of the presence of impurity in the place, so if the impurity disappears from the place, its cause has ceased. And this is because impurity disappears from the place physically, truly and legally, just as it disappears with water. His saying: [and by this] i.e., that the cause of purification is the removal of impurity, the difference between hadath and khabath is established, i.e., between legal impurity and physical impurity; for liquid does not effect purification of ghusl (ritual bath) and wudu (ablution), for vinegar removes physical impurity from the place, and the purification of the place from physical impurity by the removal of impurity has occurred, but the purification of wudu and ghusl is established legally only by using a purifier, and its cause is not the removal of impurity, because no impurity is sensed or perceived in the place to be removed; rather, vinegar only has an effect in removing impurity, nothing else, so it does not effect purification of ghusl and wudu. Regarding its removal by other than water, unlike hadath. i.e., purification of the place. It is a legal purification [in the case of physical impurity] even if it effects a physical and actual purification.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage from the hash (commentary) on Usul al-Shashi applies the usul principle that a ruling is tied to its 'illah (cause) and ceases when the 'illah ceases. The author first gives an example from zakat: the category of 'mu'allafatu qulubuhum' (those whose hearts are reconciled) was originally given zakat to attract them to Islam and strengthen Muslims. After Islam was strong, during Abu Bakr's caliphate, this was stopped because the cause (need for conciliation) had ceased. Similarly, the share for the Prophet's relatives from the khums was given for their support and loyalty; after the Prophet's death and the strengthening of Islam, this share ceased. This demonstrates that rulings based on a specific cause are impermanent. The author then provides a purification example: if a garment becomes physically impure (khabath) and is washed with vinegar, the impurity is removed and the garment becomes pure, because the cause (presence of impurity) is gone. This establishes that vinegar can purify from khabath but not from hadath (ritual impurity), because hadath has no physical presence; its removal requires specifically water (or earth) as a purifier (mutahhir). This is a Hanafi position, contrasted with al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) who reportedly does not distinguish between hadath and khabath in this regard. The lesson reinforces that understanding 'illah is central to Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
العلة (al-‘illah): The cause or effective attribute that the ruling is built upon; when it is removed, the ruling ceases.
الحدث (al-hadath): Ritual impurity (e.g., from breaking wudu or ghusl) that is not physically sensed but legally established.
الخبث (al-khabath): Physical impurity (najasa) that is perceptible to the senses and can be removed by any purifying substance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the share of the Prophet's relatives (sahm dhawi al-qurba) cease after the Prophet's death?
A) Because they no longer existed as a group.
B) Because the cause (their need for support) ceased when Islam became strong.
C) Because Abu Bakr abolished it by his own opinion.
D) Because the Quranic verse was abrogated.

Key Takeaway
Rulings in Hanafi fiqh are contingent upon their causes; when the cause ceases, the ruling ceases.

Mujtahid's Procedure When Evidences Conflict: Hierarchy and Taharrī
Explaining the hierarchy of evidences and the rule of taharrī with water/cloth example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy for resolving conflicting evidences and apply the rule of taharrī when two analogies conflict.

Core Idea
When proofs conflict, the mujtahid climbs a ladder: Sunnah, then Companions' rulings, then qiyas — and only at the last rung does taharrī decide.

Ijtihad often involves weighing proofs that appear equally strong. The Hanafi school provides a clear hierarchy: first seek resolution through the Sunnah, then the statements of the Companions, then through analogy. Only when two analogies conflict and no external preference exists does the mujtahid resort to taharrī—a personal but disciplined inner conviction. This lesson walks through that hierarchy and its practical application using the classic example of a traveler with two vessels or cloths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Type of Conflict
Determine whether the conflicting evidences are primary texts (Quran/Sunnah) or derived proofs like qiyas. The hierarchy applies differently: for primary texts, look to Sunnah for preference; for qiyas, go to taharrī after exhausting higher levels.
The passage begins: 'when two evidences conflict... he inclines to the Sunnah' — this refers to primary evidences.
2
Apply the Hierarchy
If no preference is found in the Sunnah, then turn to the effects of the Companions (athar), then to sound analogy (qiyas saḥīḥ). Each step is an attempt to find an external indication that weighs one evidence over another.
The order: Sunnah → Athar → Qiyas. This reflects the Hanafi principle of relying on transmitted knowledge before reasoning.
3
Resolve Qiyas Conflict with Taharrī
When two analogies conflict and no external preference exists, the mujtahid must perform taharrī—a sincere attempt to determine the correct ruling by inner conviction—and then act upon one of them. This is because there is no scriptural evidence below qiyas.
Taharrī is not arbitrary; it requires knowledge and a conscious effort to seek truth.
4
Note the Substitute Exception
Taharrī is only permitted when no substitute (badal) exists for the action in question. For example, water has a substitute (tayammum), so no taharrī between pure and impure water; but cloth has no substitute, so taharrī is required.
This nuance is drawn from the water/cloth example in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل الواجب على المجتهد: أنه إذا تعارض دليلان ولا مرجح لأحدهما بالدلالة أو القوة فإنه يميل إلى السنة، وإن كان بين السنتين يميل إلى آثار الصحابة رضي الله عنهم، ثم إلى القياس الصحيح. ثم إذا تعارض القياسان عند المجتهد يتحرى ويعمل بأحدهما؛ لأنه ليس دون القياس دليل شرعي يصار إليه. وعلى هذا قلنا: إذا كان مع المسافر إناءان أحدهما طاهر والآخر نجس لا يتحرى بينهما بل يتيمم؛ لأن للماء بدلاً وهو التراب. ولو كان معه ثوبان طاهر ونجس يتحرى بينهما؛ لأن للثوب بدل. ثبت بهذا أن العمل بالرأي إنما يكون عند انعدام دليل سواه.
Chapter: The duty of the mujtahid: that when two evidences conflict and there is no preference for one over the other in indication or strength, he inclines to the Sunnah, and if between two Sunnahs he inclines to the effects of the Companions, then to sound analogy. Then if two analogies conflict, the mujtahid exercises taharrī and acts on one, because there is no legal proof below analogy to resort to. Based on this we say: if a traveler has two vessels, one pure and one impure, he does not exercise taharrī between them but performs tayammum, because water has a substitute which is earth. But if he has two cloths, pure and impure, he exercises taharrī between them because a cloth has no substitute. By this it is established that acting by opinion is only when there is no other evidence.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage from the hashia of Usul al-Shashi explains the procedure for a mujtahid when faced with conflicting evidences. It first establishes a hierarchy: when two primary evidences (like Quranic verses or hadiths) conflict, the mujtahid first seeks preference via the Sunnah (hadith), then via the sayings of the Companions (athar), then via qiyas (analogy). When two qiyases conflict, he resorts to taharrī—a personal inclination verified by internal conviction—and acts on one, because there is no scriptural evidence below qiyas. The text then gives a concrete fiqh example: if a traveler has two water containers, one pure and one impure, he does not do taharrī but rather performs tayammum (dry ablution) because water has a substitute (earth). However, if he has two cloths (e.g., for covering during prayer), one pure and one impure, he does do taharrī because cloth has no substitute; he must wear one and act on his best judgment. The conclusion stresses that resorting to personal opinion (ra'y) and taharrī is only permissible when no other legal proof exists. This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on systematic preference rules in ijtihad.

Key Terms
تحري (taharrī): Exercising personal discretion and inclination of the heart to choose one of two conflicting evidences when no external preference exists
أثر (athar): Reports or rulings from the Companions of the Prophet (saw) used as secondary evidence
بدل (badal): Substitute; an alternative legal ruling or action that takes the place of the original when it is unavailable or impure

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a mujtahid do when two qiyases conflict?
A) Choose whichever is easier
B) Perform tayammum
C) Exercise taharrī and act on one
D) Wait for further revelation

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method demands systematic exhaustion of external preferences—from Sunnah to qiyas—before allowing the mujtahid's personal inclination only as a last resort.

Qiyas as a Valid Source of Law: Definition and Proof
Defining qiyas and proving its authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that qiyas is a valid proof, identify the hadith of Mu'adh as primary evidence, and explain the Hanafi response to the objection that the Quran is complete.

Core Idea
Qiyas uncovers the ruling implicit in the texts—it does not invent new law.

The Hanafi school affirms qiyas (analogical reasoning) as a legitimate source of Shari'ah when no explicit text from Quran or Sunnah is found. This lesson unpacks the definition of qiyas, the primary proof from the Prophet's approval of Mu'adh's ijtihad, and the refutation of objections raised by those who reject qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of qiyas
Start with the lexical meaning (estimation) and then the technical definition: extending the ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause (illa). Note that the ruling remains in the original; it is not transferred away.
The commentary clarifies that ta'diyat does not remove the ruling from the asl; it establishes it in the far' as well.
2
Identify the primary evidence: Hadith of Mu'adh
The Prophet asked Mu'adh how he would judge in Yemen. Mu'adh replied: by the Book, then Sunnah, then ijtihad. The Prophet approved. This ijtihad includes qiyas, so the hadith proves qiyas is valid when no text exists.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala) in supporting qiyas.
3
Address the objection from Quranic completeness
Opponents (Rawafid, Khawarij) cite Quran 16:89 that the Book clarifies everything. The Hanafi response: qiyas uncovers (kashif) what is already in the Book; it does not add new rulings.
The ruling is already implicit; qiyas makes it explicit.
4
Refute the objection from verse 4:59
Opponents say 'refer it to Allah and the Messenger' means only to text. The Hanafi response: referring a dispute to the text requires analogy (tamthil) to find similarity between the new case and the text. Thus qiyas is inherently part of referral.
The command to refer implies using qiyas to connect new cases to texts.
5
Recognize the consensus of Companions
The passage cites Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and Ibn Mas'ud who similarly instructed judges to use ijtihad (including qiyas) if no text is found. This shows the Companions unanimously accepted qiyas.
Ijma of Sahaba is a strong proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البحث الرابع في القياس هو في اللغة التقدير يقال قس بالنعل. ١٢ فصل القياس حجة أي اعتقاده. ١٢ (۲) فصل القياس حجة من حجج الشرع يجب العمل به عند انعدام ما فوقه من الدليل في الحادثة وقد ورد في ذلك الأخبار والآثار قال عليه الصلاة والسلام لمعاذ بن جبل حين بعثه الى "اليمن" قال: «بم تقضي يا معاذ؟ قال بكتاب الله تعالى قال : فان لم تجد قال بسنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه والسلام قال: فان لم تجد أجتهد برأيك». أي معاذ بن جبل. ١٢ أي آثار الصحابة والتابعين. ١٢ (۱) قوله: [في القياس هو تعدية الحكم من الأصل إلى الفرع بعلة متحدة بينهما ولا تدرك بمجرد اللغـــة، فإن قلت: إنّ التعدية توجب أن لا يبقى الحكم في الأصل؛ لأنها نقل الشيء من موضع إلى موضع آخر، قلت: إنها لا توجب عدم بقائه في الأصل ألا ترى أن تعدية الفعل هي أن لا يقتصر بالفاعل بل يتعلّق بالمفعول كما هو متعلّق بالفاعل، فالمراد هاهنا أن لا يقتصر ذلك النوع من الحكـ الحكم على الأصل بل يثبت في الفرع أيضاً، كذا في "المعدن" ۱۲ (۲) قوله: [يجب العمل به] وهذا مذهب جميع الصحابة والتابعين وعلماء الأمة في كـل عـصـر خلافاً لبعض أهل الهواء كالروافض والخوارج ؛ لأنّ الله تعالى قال : وَنَزَّلْنَا عَلَيْكَ الْكِتَابَ تِبْيَاناً لِّكُلِّ شَيْءٍ﴾ [النحل : ۸۹] فلا يحتاج إلى القياس والجواب: أن القياس كاشف عما في الكتاب ولا يكون مبيناً له، فكان المثبت هو القياس في الحقيقة، ولأنّ الله تعالى قال: فإن تَنَازَعْتُمْ فِي شَيْءٍ فَرُدُّوهُ إِلَى اللهِ وَالرَّسُولِ الآية [النساء : ٥٩] فقالوا: وجب ردّ المختلف إلى الكتاب والسنّة دون القياس، وأجيب بأنّ ردّ المختلف إلى المنصوص عليه إنّمــا يكـــون بالتمثيل أي: طلب المماثلة بين الأصل والفرع والبناء عليه وهو القياس ويؤيد ذلك الأمر بالردّ بعد الأمر بطاعة الله وطاعة رسوله عليه السلام، فإنّه يدلّ على أنّ الأحكام ثلاثة مثبـت بالكتاب والسنّة ومثبت بالردّ إليهما على وجه القياس، كذا في "البيضاوي". ١٢ (۳) قوله : المعاذ بن جبل... آه] وقال أبو موسى الأشعري حين وجهه إلى "اليمن" : اقض بكتاب الله تعالى، فإن لم تجد فبسنة رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وآله وسلّم، فإن لم تجد فاجتهد برأيك، وقال عليه السلام لابن مسعود رضي الله تعالى عنه: «اقض بالكتاب والسنّة إذا وجدتهما فإن لم تجد الحكم فيهما فاجتهد برأيك»، كذا في "كشف "المنار". ١٢
The fourth research: On Qiyas. Lexically it means estimation; it is said: measure the sandal. Section: Qiyas is a proof, i.e., belief in it. (2) Section: Qiyas is a proof among the proofs of the Shari'ah; it is obligatory to act upon it when there is no evidence above it in the incident. Reports and traditions have come regarding that. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Mu'adh ibn Jabal when he sent him to Yemen: 'By what will you judge, O Mu'adh?' He said: 'By the Book of Allah.' He said: 'If you do not find?' He said: 'By the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah.' He said: 'If you do not find?' He said: 'I will exert my opinion (ijtihad).' Meaning Mu'adh ibn Jabal. Meaning the reports of the Companions and the Followers. (1) His saying: [Qiyas is the extension of the ruling from the original to the branch by a shared effective cause that is not grasped by mere language. If you say: 'Extension necessitates that the ruling does not remain in the original, because it is transferring something from one place to another,' I say: 'It does not necessitate its non-remaining in the original. Do you not see that the transitivity of an action is that it is not restricted to the doer but attaches to the object as it attaches to the doer? So the meaning here is that that type of ruling is not restricted to the original but is established in the branch as well.' As in al-Ma'dan. (2) His saying: [It is obligatory to act upon it] This is the madhhab of all the Companions, the Followers, and the scholars of the Ummah in every age, contrary to some people of desire such as the Rawafid and the Khawarij. Because Allah said: 'And We have sent down to you the Book as clarification for all things' (16:89), so there is no need for qiyas. The answer: Qiyas uncovers what is in the Book and does not clarify it, so the establisher is qiyas in reality. And because Allah said: 'If you dispute over anything, refer it to Allah and the Messenger' (4:59). They said: It is obligatory to refer dispute to the Book and Sunnah, not to qiyas. The answer: Referring the disputed to the text is only by analogy, i.e., seeking similarity between the original and the branch and building upon it, which is qiyas. This is supported by the command to refer after the command to obey Allah and His Messenger, indicating that rulings are of three types: established by the Book and Sunnah, and established by referring to them via qiyas. As in al-Baydawi. (3) His saying: [Mu'adh ibn Jabal... etc.] And Abu Musa al-Ash'ari said when he was sent to Yemen: 'Judge by the Book of Allah, if not find, then by the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, if not find, then exert your opinion.' And the Prophet said to Ibn Mas'ud: 'Judge by the Book and Sunnah if you find them; if you do not find the ruling therein, then exert your opinion.' As in Kashf al-Manar.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage introduces the fourth research on qiyas (analogical reasoning). It begins with a lexical definition: qiyas means estimation or measuring. The section then states that qiyas is a proof (hujja) of Shari'ah; it is obligatory to act upon it when no explicit text (nass) from Quran or Sunnah exists. The primary evidence is the hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal, where the Prophet approved his plan to use ijtihad (which includes qiyas) if he found no text. The commentary addresses objections from those who reject qiyas, such as the Rawafid and Khawarij, who argue that the Quran is a complete clarification. The response is that qiyas uncovers what is already implicit in the texts. Another objection from the verse 'refer it to Allah and the Messenger' is answered by noting that referring to the text necessarily involves analogy (tamthil) to find similarity. The passage also cites Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and Ibn Mas'ud to show the consensus of the Companions on using ijtihad and qiyas. The definition in the footnote explains qiyas as extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause (illa).

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause (illa).
الحجة (al-hujja): A proof from the Shari'ah that must be followed.
تعدية الحكم (ta'diyat al-hukm): Extending the ruling from the original to the branch without removing it from the original.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary hadith used to prove the validity of qiyas according to the passage?
A) The hadith of Abu Hurairah about intention.
B) The hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal when sent to Yemen.
C) The hadith of Ibn Abbas about takbirs.
D) The hadith of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari about judgment.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a valid proof in Hanafi usul; it uncovers the ruling implicit in the texts and is necessary for deriving law for new cases.
