Qiyas as a Proof: Evidence from the Sunnah and Scholarly Consensus
Introducing qiyas as a valid legal proof with definition and evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the evidence for qiyas as a legal proof and evaluate the counterarguments from opposing groups.

Core Idea
Qiyas is a disciplined proof; the Prophet's approval of Mu'adh's ijtihad establishes it as a source when texts are absent.

This lesson introduces qiyas as a valid legal proof (hujja) in the Shari'a. We will explore its linguistic and technical definitions, examine the primary evidence from the Prophet's approval of Mu'adh's use of ijtihad, and consider the story of the Khath'ami woman. We will also address objections from those who reject qiyas and understand the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the definition
Understand that qiyas linguistically means estimation or measurement, and technically means applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a common effective cause (illa).
2
Cite the primary evidence: Hadith of Mu'adh
The Prophet asked Mu'adh how he would judge. Mu'adh replied with Quran, then Sunnah, then ijtihad. The Prophet approved, showing ijtihad (interpreted as qiyas) is valid when no text exists.
This hadith is considered proof by the majority, including Hanafis.
3
Analyze the secondary evidence: Story of the Khath'ami woman
The Prophet used analogy when asked about performing Hajj on behalf of an old man. He compared it to paying a debt, showing qiyas is used by the Prophet himself.
This demonstrates qiyas in action.
4
Evaluate opposing arguments
Some groups reject qiyas citing Quranic verses. The Hanafi response is that qiyas uncovers what is in the text; it does not add new rulings. The command to refer to Allah and the Messenger includes seeking similarity (tamthil) which is qiyas.
The author sides with the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البحث الرابع في القياس هو في اللغة التقدير يقال قس بالنعل. فصل القياس حجة أي اعتقاده. (۲) فصل القياس حجة من حجج الشرع يجب العمل به عند انعدام ما النصوص. هذا هو مذهب الجمهور. أي في حجية القياس. من النبي عليه السلام. فوقه من الدليل في الحادثة وقد ورد في ذلك الأخبار والآثار قال عليه بيان لما. رضي الله عنه . أي معاذ بن جبل. أي آثار الصحابة والتابعين. الصلاة والسلام لمعاذ بن جبل حين بعثه الى اليمن قال: بم تقضي يا معاذ؟ معاذ في الجواب أقضى. أي أرسله. الحكم المطلوب في كتاب الله تعالى فيم تقضي. قال بكتاب الله تعالى قال : فان لم تجد قال بسنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : فإن لم تجد، قال أجتهد برأيي، فصوّبه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: الحمد لله الذي وفق رسول رسول الله على ما يحب ويرضاه. وذلك في حجة الوداع. منسوبة إلى خثم وهو قبيلة. وروي أن إمرأة خَثعَميّة أتت إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت: إنّ أبي كان شيخاً كبيراً أدركه الحج ولا يستمسك على الراحلة أفيجزتني أن أحج عنه؟ قال عليه السلام: أرأيت لو كان على أبيك دين فقضيته أما كان ذلك الدين؟
The fourth discussion on qiyas. In language it is estimation; one says 'measure with the sandal'. Chapter: Qiyas is a proof—i.e., belief in it. (2) Chapter: Qiyas is a proof from the proofs of the Shari'a; it is obligatory to act upon it when texts are absent. This is the doctrine of the majority. That is, regarding the authority of qiyas. From the Prophet, peace be upon him. Above it from the evidence in the incident, and reports and traditions have come concerning that. He said, clarification of what... May Allah be pleased with him, i.e., Mu'adh ibn Jabal. i.e., the traditions of the Companions and Successors. Peace and blessings upon Mu'adh ibn Jabal when he sent him to Yemen, he said: 'By what will you judge, O Mu'adh?' Mu'adh replied, 'I will judge.' He said, 'The desired ruling in the Book of Allah, by what will you judge?' He said, 'By the Book of Allah.' He said, 'If you do not find (it)?' He said, 'By the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah.' He said, 'If you do not find (it)?' He said, 'I will exert my opinion (ijtihad).' So the Messenger of Allah approved him and said: 'Praise be to Allah who has guided the messenger of the Messenger of Allah to what He loves and is pleased with.' That was during the Farewell Pilgrimage. Attributed to Khatham, which is a tribe. And it is narrated that a woman from Khatham came to the Messenger of Allah and said: 'My father is a very old man, he is overtaken by Hajj and cannot stay on the riding animal; will it suffice if I perform Hajj on his behalf?' He said: 'Tell me, if your father had a debt and you paid it, would that discharge the debt?'
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage establishes qiyas (analogical reasoning) as a valid proof in Islamic jurisprudence according to the majority of scholars, including the Hanafi school. The author begins by giving the linguistic definition: qiyas means estimation or measurement. The legal definition, as understood from the broader context, is applying a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a common effective cause ('illa). The passage then asserts that qiyas is a proof (hujja) that must be acted upon when no explicit text from the Quran or Sunnah exists. This is the position of the majority (jumhur) of the Companions and later scholars, contrary to a few deviant groups like the Rawafid and Khawarij. To prove this, the author first cites the famous hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal when the Prophet sent him to Yemen. The Prophet asked Mu'adh how he would judge. Mu'adh replied: first by the Book of Allah, then by the Sunnah, and if no text is found, he would exert his own opinion (ijtihad). The Prophet approved and praised Allah for guiding Mu'adh. This approval demonstrates the legitimacy of qiyas, as ijtihad in the absence of text is understood to mean qiyas. The author also mentions the story of the Khath'ami woman: her father was old and unable to perform Hajj, so she asked if she could perform Hajj on his behalf. The Prophet replied by analogy: if her father had a debt, would she pay it? When she said yes, the Prophet indicated that the debt to Allah (Hajj) is more deserving to be paid. This shows the Prophet himself used qiyas, thus establishing its authority. The commentary (hashiya) addresses potential objections: some argue that the Quran says it explains everything, so qiyas is unnecessary; the response is that qiyas uncovers what is already in the Book. Another objection from the verse 'If you dispute, refer it to Allah and the Messenger' is answered by saying that referring to the text requires analogy (tamthil), which is qiyas. The hadith of Mu'adh is further defended against criticisms of its chain, noting that it is well-known (mashhur) and accepted by the umma.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): In language: estimation; in legal terminology: applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a common cause (illa).
حجة (hujja): Proof or evidence; a source of law that is binding.
النصوص (al-nusus): Explicit texts from the Quran and Sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Consensus of the Khawarij
D) The linguistic definition of qiyas

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a binding proof (hujja) in Islamic law, established by the Sunnah of the Prophet and accepted by the majority of scholars.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Qiyas as a Binding Proof (Hujja) – Evidence from the Sunnah
Three hadith proofs for qiyas as a hujja.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three hadith proofs for qiyas, explain their wajh al-dalalah, and evaluate the Hanafi defense against objections to the hadith of Mu'adh.

Core Idea
The Prophet ﷺ approved of qiyas in multiple hadiths, establishing it as a binding source when text is absent.

This lesson examines the Hanafi usul position that qiyas (analogical reasoning) is a valid and binding proof (hujja) in Islamic law. The passage presents three prophetic hadiths and their commentaries, demonstrating how the Prophet ﷺ and his Companions used analogical reasoning. Understanding these proofs is essential for grasping the Hanafi methodology of legal derivation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three hadiths
List each hadith: (1) Hadith of Mu'adh, where the Prophet approves of ijtihad. (2) Hadith of the Khath'ami woman about Hajj on behalf of her father, analogized to debt. (3) Hadith of the Bedouin asking about touching the penis, answered by analogy to other body parts. Note the narrators and context.
These hadiths come from different Companions and scenarios.
2
Analyze the first hadith: Hadith of Mu'adh
This is the primary proof. The Prophet's approval of Mu'adh's statement 'I will exert my own opinion (ijtihad)' is taken as endorsement of qiyas, since ijtihad in the absence of text means qiyas. Address the objection about its chain (munqati') and the Hanafi response that it is mashhur and accepted by the ummah.
Al-Ghazali considered it almost mutawatir due to acceptance.
3
Analyze the second hadith: Hajj by proxy analogized to debt
The Prophet explicitly draws an analogy between a financial debt and a religious duty (Hajj). The common effective cause ('illa) is fulfillment (qada'). This demonstrates qiyas from a textual example.
The commentary explains the linguistic difference between 'bala' and 'na'am'.
4
Analyze the third hadith: Touching the penis
The Prophet says 'Is it but a piece of him?' meaning the penis is like any other body part. Thus, touching it does not break wudu. This ruling is derived by qiyas: since other body parts do not nullify wudu upon touch, the penis is analogized to them.
This hadith is also used by Hanafis to support the ruling on wudu.
5
Synthesize the overall proof
Together, these hadiths establish that qiyas is a valid method when no explicit text exists. The Hanafi position is that qiyas is a hujja (binding proof) for deriving rulings, supported by prophetic practice and explicit approval.
The passage also references the practice of the Companions and their use of qiyas.

Source Text

فصل القياس حجة
عن معاذ بن جبل رضي الله عنه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لما بعثه إلى اليمن قال: بم تحكم؟ قال: بكتاب الله. قال: فإن لم تجد؟ قال: بسنة رسول الله. قال: فإن لم تجد؟ قال: أجتهد برأيي. فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: الحمد لله الذي وفق رسول رسول الله لما يحب ويرضاه.
(قوله: [أجتهد ... إلخ] فإن قلت : الاجتهاد ليس نفس القياس بل الاجتهاد استفراغ الجهد في الطلب فيحمل على طلب الحكم من النصوص الخفيّة أو على القياس الذي علّته منصوصة، قلت: إنّ الاجتهاد فيما نحن فيه هو القياس الشرعي؛ لأنّ الاجتهاد في الحوادث التي لم يجد حكمها في الكتاب والسنة ليس إلا القياس الشرعي، فإن قيل: كان هذا في ابتداء الإسلام حين كان في المنصوص قلّة فدعت الحاجة إلى القياس، فإذا فات الشرط فات المشروط، أجيب: بأنا لانسلّم أنه كان في ابتداء الإســـلام ولئن سلّمنا فالحاجة الداعية إلى القياس إنما هي خلوّ الحادثة عن النص ونحن لا تجوز القياس إلا عنــــد فقدان النصّ فيقتضي مشروعيّة القياس وهو المطلوب فافهم، كذا في "المعدن".)
(قوله: [فصوبه ... إلخ] فتصويبه صلّى الله تعالى عليه وآله وسلّم لمعاذ رضي الله تعالى عنه وحمــــده الله تعالى دليل صريح على جواز العمل بالقياس عند فقدان النص من الكتاب والسنة، فإنّه لـو لم يكـــن القياس حجّة موجبة للعمل بعد الكتاب والسنّة لأنكره عليه السلام، وفي الحديث دلالة قوية على جواز القياس وردّ قبيح على من أنكرها أصلاً.)
(قوله: [فصوبه... إلخ] قال الترمذي في جامعه: هذا حديث لا نعرفه إلا من هذا الوجه وليس إسناده عندنا بمتصل، قلت: وبمثل هذا الجرح ليس حرجاً معتبراً، فإنّ الانقطاع كالإرسال غير جرح كما قال ابن الهمام رحمه الله تعالى عنه والمستور من المقرون الثلاثة كالعدل عندنا من الثقاة، ثُمّ هذا الحديث عدّه أهل الأصول من المشاهير مرتقياً من الآحاد، وقال الغزالي: تلقته الأمة بالقبول فصار كالمتواتر فلا شك في كونه من المشاهير، والله أعلم.)
(قوله: [الحمد لله الذي... آه] فلو لم يكن القياس حجّةً موجبة للعمل بعد الكتاب والسنة لأنكر عليه رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وآله وسلّم وإذا مدحه به حمد الله بتوفيقه لمعاذ بالعمل والاجتهاد ودلّ على أنه حجة موجبة للعمل عند عدم النص من الكتاب والسنّة، كذا في "المعدن".)
وروي أن امرأة خثعمية أتت إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت: إن أبي كان شيخاً كبيراً أدركه الحج ولا يستمسك على الراحلة أفيجزئني أن أحج عنه؟ قال عليه السلام: أرأيت لو كان على أبيك دين فقضيته أكان يجزيءك؟ قالت: بلى. قال: فدين الله أحق وأولى.
(قوله: [بلى] الفرق بين «بلى» و«نعم» أنّ موجب «نعم» تصديق ما قبله من الكلام منفياً كان أو مثبتاً استفهاماً كان أو خبراً كما إذا قيل لك: «أقام زيد أو لم يقم؟» فقلت: «نعم» كان تصديقاً لما قبلــــه وتخصيصاً لما بعد الهمزة، وموجب «بلى» إيجاب ما بعد النفي استفهاماً كان أو خبراً، فإذا قيل: « لم يقم زيد فقلت: «بلى» كان معناه قد قام»، وقد يستعمل أحدهما مكان الآخر.)
(قوله: [وهذا] أي إلحاق الحجّ بالحقوق المالية مع بيان العلّة المؤثّرة المشتركة وهي القضاء.)
(قوله: [وروي] ورواه محمّد ابن الحسن الشيباني في "مؤطا" وابن حبان في صحيحه وقال الطحاوي: مستقيم الإسناد، وروي أنّ عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه سأل النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام عن قبلة الصائم، فقال: «لو تمضمضت ثُمّ محجت أكان يضرك؟» وعمل الصحابة ومناظراتهم في القياس أشهر من أن يخفى.)
وروي ابن الصباغ في كتابه المسمى بـ«الشامل» عن قيس بن طلق بن علي أنه قال: «جاء رجل إلى رسول الله عليه السلام كأنه بدوي فقال يا نبي الله ما ترى في مس الرجل ذكره بعد ما توضأ فقال: هل هو إلا بضعة منه».
(قوله: [وروي ابن الصباغ ... إلخ] أقول وأيضاً روى هذا الحديث أصحاب السنن إلا ابن ماجة عن ملازم بن عمرو عن عبد بن بدر عن قيس بن طلق بن علي عن أبيه عن النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلّم أنه سئل عن الرجل بمس ذكره في الصلاة، فقال: «هل هو إلا بصنعه منك» ورواه ابن حبّان في صحيحه، وقال الترمذي: هذا الحديث أحسن شيء يروي في هذا الباب، وفي الباب عن أبي أمامة بن الحسن الشيباني في "مؤطاه" قال : أخبرنا أيوب بن عتبة التميمي قاضي اليمامة من قيس ابن طلق أن أباه حدثه أنّ رجلاً سأل رسول الله صلّى الله تعالى عليه وسلّم عن رجل مس ذكـــره أيتوضأ قال : «هل هو إلاّ بضعة من جسدك».)
(قوله: [إلا بضعة منه ... إلخ] وفي رواية «مضغة منه» أي : مسه كمس عضو وجزء آخر من البدن في انتقاض الطهارة.)
Section: Qiyas is a Proof. From Mu'adh ibn Jabal that the Prophet ﷺ when he sent him to Yemen said: 'By what will you judge?' He said: 'By the Book of Allah.' He said: 'If you do not find (a ruling)?' He said: 'By the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah.' He said: 'If you do not find?' He said: 'I will exert my own opinion (ijtihad).' The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Praise be to Allah who has guided the messenger of the Messenger of Allah to what pleases Him.' (Commentary: This shows qiyas is valid when no text exists, and the hadith is defended against criticism of weakness.) And it is narrated that a woman from Khath'am came to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ and said: 'My father is an old man who has reached (the age of) Hajj but cannot stay on the mount. Does it suffice if I perform Hajj on his behalf?' He said: 'What do you think, if your father had a debt and you paid it, would it suffice?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Then the debt of Allah is more deserving (of being fulfilled).' (Commentary: This applies qiyas by analogy from financial debts to religious duties, and the hadith is authentic.) And Ibn al-Sabbagh narrated in his book 'al-Shamil' from Qays ibn Talq ibn Ali that he said: 'A man came to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ as if he were a Bedouin and said: O Prophet of Allah, what do you say about a man touching his penis after performing wudu? He said: Is it anything but a piece of him?' (Commentary: This shows that touching the penis does not invalidate wudu, derived by qiyas that it is like any other body part.)
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage presents the usul rule that qiyas (analogical reasoning) is a valid proof (hujja) in Islamic law. The author of the matn begins by citing three prophetic hadiths. The first is the famous hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal, where the Prophet ﷺ explicitly approved of Mu'adh's intention to use his own reasoning (ijtihad) when no ruling is found in the Quran or Sunnah. The commentary clarifies that ijtihad here refers specifically to qiyas, since there is no other method of deriving rulings for new cases when texts are silent. It also addresses objections, such as the claim that this was only allowed in early Islam due to few texts, by stating that the need for qiyas remains whenever a case has no textual ruling. The commentary further defends the hadith against criticism from al-Tirmidhi, who said its chain is disconnected; the commentator argues that such discontinuity is not a fatal flaw and that the hadith is widely accepted (mashhur) and treated as nearly mutawatir. The second hadith involves a woman asking about performing Hajj on behalf of her elderly father. The Prophet ﷺ analogized the obligation of Hajj to a financial debt, thereby establishing that qiyas is a valid method for extending rulings. The commentary explains that the common effective cause ('illa) is 'payment' or 'fulfillment' (qada'), which applies to both debts and religious duties. The third hadith concerns a man touching his penis after wudu; the Prophet ﷺ said it is merely a piece of his body, implying that touching it does not break wudu. The commentary notes that this ruling is derived by qiyas—since the penis is part of the body like any other limb, its touch does not nullify purity unless specified. All three hadiths, along with the extensive commentary, firmly establish the Hanafi position that qiyas is a legitimate source of law, to be used when no explicit text exists.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a shared effective cause ('illa).
حجة (hujja): A proof or evidence that is binding and must be followed in deriving legal rulings.
اجتهاد (ijtihad): Exerting maximum effort to derive a ruling; in this context, it specifically refers to qiyas when no text exists.
مشهور (mashhur): A hadith that is widely transmitted but not reaching mutawatir; in Hanafi usul, it is considered strong enough to establish a ruling.
منقطع (munqati'): A hadith with a disconnected chain (one or more narrators omitted).
مرسل (mursal): A hadith where a Successor narrates directly from the Prophet, omitting the Companion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the hadith of Mu'adh, what did the Prophet ﷺ say when Mu'adh stated he would use his own opinion (ijtihad)?
A) He remained silent.
B) He said: 'Praise be to Allah who has guided the messenger of the Messenger of Allah to what pleases Him.'
C) He said: 'You are wrong; use only the Quran.'
D) He said: 'That is not permissible.'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on multiple hadith to establish qiyas as a legitimate source, supported by the Prophet's explicit approval and the practice of Companions.

Qiyas as a Proof: The Hadith of the Woman and the Debt
Demonstrates qiyas using the Prophet's analogy from financial debt to religious duty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Prophet's analogy in the hadith of the woman and the debt establishes qiyas as a valid source of law in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
The Prophet used qiyas to compare debts to religious duties, proving qiyas is a legitimate source.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi argues that qiyas (analogical reasoning) is a valid proof (hujja) in Islamic law. The author cites a hadith where a woman asked the Prophet if paying her father's debt would suffice, and the Prophet replied, 'The debt of Allah is more deserving and foremost.' This lesson unpacks how the Prophet's statement serves as evidence for qiyas and why this matters in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Original (asl) and New (far) Cases
In the hadith, the woman asks about fulfilling her father's financial debt. The Prophet's answer shifts to the religious obligation of Hajj. Identify which is the original case (asl) and which is the new case (far').
The asl is the financial debt, the far' is Hajj.
2
Determine the Ruling in the Original Case
For a financial debt, the ruling is that it must be repaid (wajib). This is the hukm of the asl.
3
Identify the Effective Cause (illa)
What attribute makes the ruling applicable to both cases? The Prophet's response indicates the illa is 'qada' (repayment/fulfillment). Both financial debt and Hajj require performance.
The commentary explicitly calls 'qada' the effective cause.
4
Analyze the Prophet's Analogy
By saying 'the debt of Allah is more deserving and foremost,' the Prophet analogizes the woman's financial situation to the religious duty, implying that if financial repayment is required, then religious repayment is even more binding.
This is a straightforward analogical transfer (qiyas).
5
Conclude the Proof for Qiyas
The text states: 'And if it were not a correct qiyas, he would not have done it.' Therefore, the Prophet's action validates qiyas as a legitimate method of legal derivation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل القياس حجة بالوفاء والأداء عن أبيك. يجزئك، فقالت: بلى! فقال عليه السلام: «فدين الله أحق وأولى»، ألحق إشارة إلى وجه التمسك. أي الذي هو دين الله تعالى. هو الذي قريب إلى الفناء. رسول الله عليه السلام الحج في حق الشيخ الفاني بالحقوق المالية وأشار إلى هذا مقيس. أي العلة المؤثرة في الجواز. ولو لم يكن قياسا صحيحا لما فعله. عليه السلام. علّة مؤثرة في الجواز وهي القضاء وهذا هو القياس.
Chapter: Qiyas is a proof. By fulfilling and rendering from your father. It suffices you. She said: Yes. So he, peace be upon him, said: 'The debt of Allah is more deserving and foremost.' He appended an indication to the aspect of adherence. That is the debt of Allah Almighty. He is the one near to annihilation. The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, [made] Hajj in the right of the elderly man with financial rights and pointed to this measured. That is the effective cause in permissibility. And if it were not a correct qiyas, he would not have done it. Peace be upon him. An effective cause in permissibility, which is repayment, and this is qiyas.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi states that qiyas is a proof. It cites a hadith where a woman asked the Prophet if paying her father's debt would suffice. The Prophet replied, 'The debt of Allah is more deserving and foremost,' indicating that religious duties are even more important. The commentary (Ahsan al-Hawashi) explains that the Prophet used qiyas: the effective cause (illa) for permissibility is the fulfillment of a debt, which applies to both financial and religious obligations. The Prophet's action proves the validity of qiyas.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a shared effective cause (illa).
علة (illa): The effective cause that triggers the ruling; here it is 'qada' (repayment).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the hadith of the woman and the debt, what did the Prophet indicate by saying 'the debt of Allah is more deserving and foremost'?
A) That financial debts are more important than religious duties.
B) That qiyas is not allowed in religious matters.
C) That the obligation of Hajj is like a debt to Allah, so it is even more important.
D) That the woman should not pay her father's debt.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of the woman and the debt provides a prophetic precedent for qiyas, establishing it as a valid method of legal reasoning in the Hanafi school.

Qiyas as Proof: The Case of Touching the Private Part and Wudu
Uses qiyas to rule that touching the private part does not break wudu, with ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qiyas framework to derive a ruling and evaluate the strength of competing hadith in a disputed case.

Core Idea
Touching the private part does not break wudu – qiyas to other limbs, reinforced by stronger hadith.

In this passage, the author presents a classic usul al-fiqh argument that qiyas is a legitimate proof. The case is the disputed ruling on whether touching one's private part invalidates wudu. The Hanafi school uses qiyas based on a hadith, while other schools rely on a different hadith. This lesson will walk through the qiyas structure and the evidence weighing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
What is the legal ruling that is contested? The Hanafi school holds one position; the Shafi'i school holds another.
The ruling is about whether touching the private part breaks wudu.
2
Extract the qiyas structure
Identify the asl, far', and illa (common factor) used in the analogy.
Asl: other limbs; far': private part; illa: absence of impurity.
3
Identify the Hanafi dalil
What is the primary evidence for the Hanafi position? (Hadith of Talq)
The Prophet said: 'Is it not just a piece of flesh?'
4
Identify the opposing dalil
What evidence does the opposing school (Shafi'i) rely on? (Hadith of Busra)
That hadith commands renewal of wudu upon touching.
5
Evaluate the tarjih reasoning
How does the Hanafi scholar argue that their hadith is stronger?
By comparing the chain of narration: men vs. women, as per Ibn al-Humam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وروى ابن الصباغ عن قيس بن طلق بن علي أنه قال: «جاء رجل إلى رسول الله عليه السلام كأنه بدوي فقال يا نبي الله ما ترى في مس الرجل ذكره بعد ما توضأ فقال: هل هو إلا بضعة منه» وهذا هو القياس. لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قاس هذا العضو على سائر الأعضاء لا ينقض الوضوء فكذا هذا والجامع هو عدم خروج النجاسة. وقال الفلاس: «هو أثبت عندي من حديث بسرة»، قال ابن الهمام: ويترجح أيضاً بأنّ حديث الرجال أقوى من حديث النساء لنقصان في الحفظ والضبط والعقل، ولهذا جعلت شهادة امرأتين كشهادة رجل واحد فثبت من هذا الحديث أنه لا ينقض الوضوء من مس الذكر وهو مذهبنا وهو قول عمر وعلي وابن مسعود وابن عباس وعمار وزيد بن ثابت وحذيفة وعمران بن حصين وأبي الدرداء وأبي هريرة وسعد ابن أبي وقاص، وقال الطحاوي: لا نعلم أحداً من الصحابة أفتى بالوضوء منه غير ابن عمر وقد خالفه أكثرهم فيه، وقال الشافعي وأحمد وداود: يجب الوضوء منه، واختلف فيه أصحاب مالك، وقال الترمذي: هو قول غير واحد من الصحابة والتابعين وبه يقول أحمد والأوزاعي والشافعي وإسحاق، وغيرهم. كذا في 'الحصول'.
And Ibn al-Sabbagh narrated from Qays ibn Talq ibn Ali that he said: 'A man came to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, as if he was a Bedouin and said: O Prophet of Allah, what do you think about a man touching his penis after he has done wudu? He said: Is it not just a piece of flesh?' And this is qiyas. Because he, peace be upon him, analogized this limb to the rest of the limbs that do not break wudu, and the common factor is the absence of impurity. And al-Fallas said: 'It is more established in my view than the hadith of Busra.' Ibn al-Humam said: And it is also preponderant because the hadith of men is stronger than the hadith of women due to deficiency in memory, accuracy, and intellect, and for this reason the testimony of two women is made equal to the testimony of one man. So it is established from this hadith that touching the penis does not break wudu, and that is our madhhab, and it is the saying of Umar, Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Abbas, Ammar, Zaid ibn Thabit, Hudhayfa, Imran ibn Husayn, Abu al-Darda', Abu Hurayra, and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas. And al-Tahawi said: We do not know any of the Companions who gave a fatwa of wudu from it other than Ibn Umar, and the majority opposed him in it. And al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and Dawud said: Wudu is required from it. And the companions of Malik differed in it. And al-Tirmidhi said: It is the saying of many Companions and Followers, and Ahmad, al-Awza'i, al-Shafi'i, and Ishaq hold it, and others. As in 'al-Husul'.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof for qiyas: the hadith of the man who touched his private part. The Prophet replied, 'Is it not just a piece of flesh?' indicating that like any other limb, touching it does not invalidate wudu. The commentary explains that this is qiyas: the Prophet analogized the private part to other limbs. The common factor (jami') is the absence of impurity (najasa). Then a lengthy ikhtilaf is presented: The Hanafi school (our madhhab) holds that touching the private part does not break wudu, based on this hadith and the qiyas. The opposing schools (Shafi'i, Ahmad, Dawud) require wudu. The commentary also discusses the strength of the hadith compared to the hadith of Busra (which requires wudu) and concludes that the hadith of Talq is stronger because it is narrated by men (who are more reliable).

Key Terms
بضعة (buda'a): A piece of flesh; the Prophet described the private part as such.
نقض الوضوء (naqd al-wudu): Invalidating ablution; breaking the state of purity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument in this passage, why is the hadith of Talq considered stronger than the hadith of Busra?
A) It is narrated by men.
B) It is a mutawatir hadith.
C) It is supported by qiyas.
D) It is a direct command from the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses qiyas based on the hadith of Talq to rule that touching the private part does not break wudu, preferring it over the hadith of Busra due to stronger narration.

Ibn Mas'ud's Ijtihad: Qiyas as a Source of Law
Companion's ijtihad using qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Ibn Mas'ud used qiyas to derive the ruling of mahr al-mithl and identify the elements of qiyas in his ijtihad.

Core Idea
A Companion's ijtihad using qiyas is a valid source of law in Hanafi usul.

This passage presents a famous case where Ibn Mas'ud was asked about a marriage without a specified dower. His methodical deliberation and use of analogy demonstrate that qiyas was an accepted method among the Companions. We will analyze the structure of his ijtihad and identify the components of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case presented to Ibn Mas'ud
A woman married without a specified dower, and her husband died before consummation. This is the factual scenario requiring a legal ruling.
Note the absence of a specified dower is key.
2
Examine his method: deliberation and ijtihad
Ibn Mas'ud did not give an immediate answer; he asked for a month to reflect, then stated he would use his own reasoning (ra'y). This shows ijtihad is a deliberate process.
He humbly attributed correctness to Allah and error to himself.
3
Extract his ruling
He ruled that the woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl, i.e., the dower of her peers, without reduction or excess.
4
Analyze the qiyas structure
Identify the original case (asl) – women with known dowers; the new case (far') – this woman; the effective cause (illa) – the lack of specified dower; the ruling transferred (hukm) – mahr al-mithl.
The illa is that she is entitled to a dower by analogy to peers.
5
Recognize the authority level
Ibn Mas'ud's ijtihad is a qawl al-sahabi, which in Hanafi usul is a valid source (hujjah) when not opposed by another Companion.
This establishes the precedent for using qiyas in similar cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسئل ابن مسعود عمن تزوج امرأة ولم يسم لها مهرا رواه علقمة بن قيس النخعي عنه. أي طلب المهلة للتأمل في الجواب. وقد مات عنها زوجها قبل الدخول فاستمهل شهرا ثم قال: أجتهد فيه برأيي فان كان صوابا فمن الله وإن كان خطأ فمن ابن أم عبد فقال: أرى لها مهر مثل نسائها لا وكس فيها ولا شطط. كني ابن مسعود عن نفسه وأم عبد أمه.
And Ibn Mas'ud was asked about a man who married a woman and did not name a dower for her, narrated by Alqamah ibn Qays al-Nakha'i from him. He asked for a delay for reflection in the answer. And her husband had died before consummation. So he asked for a month, then said: I exert my ijtihad in it with my opinion. If it is correct, it is from Allah, and if it is wrong, it is from Ibn Umm Abd. Then he said: I think she has a dower like that of her women, no reduction and no excess. Ibn Mas'ud referred to himself as 'Ibn Umm Abd', and Umm Abd was his mother.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage demonstrates the use of qiyas and ijtihad by a Companion. Ibn Mas'ud was presented with a case: a woman married without a specified dower, and her husband died before consummation. He took a month to deliberate, then gave his opinion that she deserves the mahr al-mithl (dower of her peers), based on analogy with similar cases. He humbly attributed correctness to Allah and error to himself. This shows that qiyas was a recognized method among the Companions.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower of a woman's peers; the standard dower in similar circumstances.
اجتهاد (ijtihad): Independent legal reasoning to derive a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) She receives nothing.
B) She receives half the dower of her peers.
C) She receives the dower of her peers without reduction or excess.
D) She receives a fixed amount of 500 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
Companion's ijtihad using qiyas is a valid source in Hanafi usul.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Qiyas as a Proof: Evidence from the Practice of Ibn Mas'ud
Establishes qiyas as a proof via a Sahaba ijtihad and a hadith dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of qiyas and apply it to distinguish when qiyas is used as a proof versus when it is not.

Core Idea
Qiyas is a valid legal proof validated by Companion practice and textual analogy.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi establishes that qiyas (analogical reasoning) is a legitimate source of Islamic law. The author uses two examples: the first shows the Companion Ibn Mas'ud using ijtihad based on analogy to determine a dowry, and the second applies the same reasoning to the ruling on wudu after touching the penis. Together, they demonstrate that when no explicit text exists, qiyas provides guidance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's claim
The author begins by stating that after discussing transmitted reports (akhbar), he now turns to qiyas. The claim is that qiyas is a hujjah (proof) in Islamic law.
This is the main thesis of the passage.
2
Analyze the first evidence: Ibn Mas'ud's ijtihad
The author narrates that Ibn Mas'ud was asked about a man who married without specifying a dowry and died before consummation. Ibn Mas'ud delayed his answer for a month, then gave a ruling based on his own ijtihad: the woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the dowry of her peers). This shows that a Companion used qiyas when no direct nass existed.
The ruling was derived by analogy to similar dowry cases.
3
Analyze the second evidence: the wudu dispute
The passage then presents a dispute on whether touching the penis nullifies wudu. The Hanafi position (no nullification) is supported by a hadith (Busrah) and by qiyas: since other limbs do not nullify wudu unless there is emission, the penis is analogous. The opposing view (Shafi'i, Ahmad) requires wudu based on other hadith.
The dispute highlights how qiyas can lead to different rulings based on which analogy is preferred.
4
Understand the Hanafi tarjih
The author concludes that the Hanafi position is preferred because it is supported by a stronger hadith (according to al-Fallas) and by the practice of a majority of Companions. This illustrates the Hanafi methodology in weighing evidence.
The weight given to companion practice and hadith strength is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أصول الشاشي مع أحسن الحواشي فصل القياس حجة شرع في الآثار بعد فراغه من الأخبار وهذا هو القياس وسئل ابن مسعود عمن تزوج امرأة ولم يسم لها مهرا رواه علقمة بن قيس النخعي عنه رضي الله عنه وقد مات عنها زوجها قبل الدخول فاستمهل شهرا ثم قال أجتهد فيه برأيي فإن كان صوابا فمن الله وإن كان خطأ فمن ابن أم عبد فقال أرى لها مهر مثل نسائها لا وكس فيها ولا شطط كني ابن مسعود عن نفسه وأم عبد أمه وعدم الحدث قال الفلاس هو أثبت عندي من حديث بسرة قال ابن الهمام ويترجح أيضا بأن حديث الرجال أقوى من حديث النساء لنقصان في الحفظ والضبط والعقل ولهذا جعلت شهادة امرأتين كشهادة رجل واحد فثبت من هذا الحديث أنه لا ينقض الوضوء من مس الذكر وهو مذهبنا وهو قول عمر وعلي وابن مسعود وابن عباس وعمار وزيد بن ثابت وحذيفة وعمران بن حصين وأبي الدرداء وأبي هريرة وسعد ابن أبي وقاص وقال الطحاوي لا نعلم أحدا من الصحابة أفتى بالوضوء منه غير ابن عمر وقد خالفه أكثرهم فيه وقال الشافعي وأحمد وداود يجب الوضوء منه واختلف فيه أصحاب مالك وقال الترمذي هو قول غير واحد من الصحابة والتابعين وبه يقول أحمد والأوزاعي والشافعي وإسحاق وغيرهم كذا في الحصول
Principles of al-Shashi with the Best of Annotations. Section: Qiyas is a proof. He began with traditions after finishing reports. And this is qiyas. Ibn Mas'ud was asked about a man who married a woman and did not specify a dowry for her, narrated by 'Alqamah bin Qays al-Nakha'i from him, may Allah be pleased with him. And her husband died before consummation, so he asked for a month's delay, then said: I will exert my opinion therein. If it is correct, it is from Allah; if it is wrong, it is from Ibn Umm 'Abd. He said: I think she has the mahr of her peers, no diminution and no excess. Ibn Mas'ud referred to himself as Ibn Umm 'Abd, and Umm 'Abd is his mother. And the absence of impurity: al-Fallas said: It is more established with me than the hadith of Busrah. Ibn al-Humam said: It is also preponderated because the hadith of men is stronger than the hadith of women due to deficiency in memory, precision, and intellect, and therefore the testimony of two women is made equivalent to the testimony of one man. So it is established from this hadith that wudu is not nullified by touching the penis, and this is our madhhab, and it is the saying of 'Umar, 'Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn 'Abbas, 'Ammar, Zayd bin Thabit, Hudhayfah, 'Imran bin Husayn, Abu al-Darda', Abu Hurayrah, and Sa'd bin Abi Waqqas. Al-Tahawi said: We do not know any companion who gave a fatwa of wudu from it other than Ibn 'Umar, and most of them opposed him. Al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and Dawud said: Wudu is obligatory from it. The companions of Malik differed on it. Al-Tirmidhi said: It is the saying of more than one of the Companions and Successors, and Ahmad, al-Awza'i, al-Shafi'i, Ishaq, and others hold it. End quote from al-Husul.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi establishes qiyas as a proof (hujjah) in Islamic law. The author begins by stating that after discussing transmitted reports (akhbar), he now turns to qiyas. The primary evidence presented is the practice of the Companion Ibn Mas'ud (radiAllahu 'anhu). He was asked about a man who married a woman without specifying a dowry and then died before consummation. Ibn Mas'ud requested a month to deliberate, then declared he would exercise ijtihad. He ruled that the woman is entitled to the mahr al-mithl (the dowry of her peers) based on analogy, as he derived the ruling by comparing this case to similar situations. This demonstrates that qiyas was used by the sahabah and is thus a valid source. The passage then shifts to a fiqh dispute about whether touching the penis nullifies wudu. The author cites a hadith that it does not, and lists many Companions who held this view. The opposing view (Shafi'i, Ahmad, etc.) requires wudu. This discussion serves as an example of qiyas: the penis is compared to other limbs, and since they do not nullify wudu, this also does not, as long as there is no emission. The authority weight of the ruling (no wudu from touching) is from the practice of the Companions and the hadith, and the Hanafi position is considered zahir al-riwayah.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dowry commensurate with the woman's peers in family status, beauty, wealth, etc.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning to extend a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause.
إجماع الصحابة (ijma' al-sahabah): Consensus of the Companions on a ruling, considered a strong proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi position on wudu after touching the penis?
A) Wudu is obligatory
B) Wudu is recommended
C) Wudu is not nullified
D) Wudu is invalid

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a valid proof in Hanafi usul, as shown by the ijtihad of Ibn Mas'ud and the Hanafi position on wudu nullification, which is supported by both hadith and analogy.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
beginner
6 min
Five Conditions for the Validity of Qiyas
Lists and explains the five necessary conditions for a valid analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions for the validity of qiyas and explain why each condition prevents misuse of analogy in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Qiyas is valid only when it does not oppose a text, does not change the text's ruling, involves a rationally understood original, applies to a legal ruling, and the new case is not already ruled.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi presents the foundational gatekeeping conditions for qiyas. Without these, an analogy is not permissible in the Hanafi school. Understanding these conditions ensures that qiyas remains a servant to revelation, not a tool for arbitrary reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the five conditions in order
Read each condition carefully from the source text. Note the Arabic phrasing: 'an la yakuna fi muqabilati al-nass', etc.
The conditions are listed sequentially; each has a distinct rationale.
2
Understand the rationale behind each condition
For each condition, ask: 'Why is this necessary?' E.g., condition 1 ensures qiyas does not override clear texts; condition 2 preserves the integrity of the text's ruling; condition 3 excludes purely devotional rulings; condition 4 limits qiyas to legal matters; condition 5 avoids redundancy.
The third condition (ma'qul al-ma'na) is a key Hanafi principle: only rationally understood 'illahs can be extended.
3
Identify violations with examples
For each condition, think of a scenario where qiyas would be invalid. E.g., condition 1: analogizing a ruling that contradicts a clear Quranic verse; condition 2: changing the ruling of zakat from obligatory to recommended via analogy; condition 3: analogizing the number of rak'ahs in prayer; condition 4: analogizing a grammatical rule to a legal ruling; condition 5: applying qiyas to find a ruling for wine when the Quran already prohibits it.
These examples help internalize the boundaries.
4
Distinguish between conditions 2 and 5
Condition 2 prohibits changing the text's ruling itself (e.g., making halal into haram), while condition 5 says the new case must not already have a text ruling. Both protect the text but from different angles.
Condition 2 is about the ruling of the original case; condition 5 is about the new case.
5
Synthesize the overall purpose
The five conditions collectively ensure qiyas is a valid proof (hujjah) only when it operates within the boundaries set by revelation. They prevent personal opinion and arbitrary analogy.
This is a memorization anchor for usul students.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل شروط صحة القياس خمسة أحدها أن لا يكون في مقابلة النص والثاني أن لا يتضمن تغيير حكم من أحكام النص والثالث أن لا يكون المعدى حكما لا يعقل معناه والرابع أن يقع التعليل لحكم شرعي لا لأمر لغوي والخامس أن لا يكون الفرع منصوصا عليه
Section: Conditions of the validity of qiyas are five: First, that it does not oppose a text; Second, that it does not entail changing a ruling from the rulings of the text; Third, that the basis (original) is not a ruling whose meaning is not understood rationally; Fourth, that the reasoning (ta'lil) occurs for a legal ruling, not for a linguistic matter; Fifth, that the branch (new case) is not itself explicitly ruled upon in the text.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi presents the five necessary conditions for qiyas to be valid in Hanafi usul. 1) Qiyas must not contradict a clear text (nass) from Quran or Sunnah. If it does, the text takes precedence. 2) Qiyas must not change the ruling of the text itself; it only extends it to new cases. 3) The original ruling (hukm al-asl) must be rationally understood (ma'qul al-ma'na). Rulings that are purely devotional (ta'abbudi) cannot be analogized. 4) The 'illah (effective cause) must be for a legal ruling (hukm shar'i), not for a linguistic rule (amr lughawi). Grammatical analogies do not produce legal rulings. 5) The new case (far') must not already have a ruling from a clear text; if it does, qiyas is unnecessary or invalid. These conditions ensure that qiyas operates within the boundaries of revelation and reason. The commentary expands on each: e.g., the first condition prohibits qiyas against a sahih text; the second permits changes in scope (from particular to general) but not in the essence of the ruling; the third requires the 'illah to be known; the fourth distinguishes legal from linguistic reasoning; the fifth prevents redundancy.

Key Terms
النص (al-nass): A clear text from Quran or Sunnah that is explicit and authoritative
التعليل (al-ta'lil): The process of identifying an effective cause ('illah) for a ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which condition prevents qiyas from being applied to purely linguistic matters?
A) First condition: not opposing a text
B) Second condition: not changing the ruling
C) Third condition: original ruling must be rationally understood
D) Fourth condition: ta'lil must be for a legal ruling

Key Takeaway
The five conditions ensure that qiyas remains a valid yet restricted tool, always subordinate to revealed texts.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Five Conditions for the Validity of Qiyas
Listing and explaining the five conditions for valid qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions for valid qiyas and apply them to evaluate whether a given qiyas is valid according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Qiyas is invalid if it contradicts a clear text, changes the ruling, or if the branch is already ruled by nass.

In Hanafi usul, qiyas is a source of law, but it is subject to strict conditions. This passage from Usul al-Shashi enumerates five conditions that must be met for qiyas to be valid. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly applying analogical reasoning and avoiding invalid extensions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first condition: qiyas must not oppose a textual proof (nass).
If a clear text from Quran or Sunnah directly addresses the branch case, qiyas cannot contradict it. Example: the hadith on laughter in prayer overrides any qiyas regarding nullification of wudu.
This condition is fundamental to preserve the primacy of revelation.
2
Identify the second condition: qiyas must not involve changing a ruling of the textual proofs.
Qiyas cannot alter the essential meaning of a text, e.g., by making a general ruling specific or vice versa. This preserves the original ruling's integrity.
The change referred to is in the meaning (mafhum), not in scope (takhsis), which is natural in ta'lil.
3
Identify the third condition: the transferred ruling (from original case) must be rationally comprehensible.
If the original ruling's rationale ('illa) is not understood rationally, qiyas cannot be applied. This excludes purely devotional rulings (ta'abbudi) like the number of rak'at.
The original ruling must be proven by one of the three primary sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma), not by another qiyas.
4
Identify the fourth condition: ta'lil (attribution of cause) must be for a legal ruling, not a linguistic one.
Qiyas is a legal tool; it cannot be used to establish linguistic meanings or grammatical rules. This distinguishes qiyas shari'i from qiyas lughawi.
Some Shafi'is allow linguistic qiyas, but the Hanafi position restricts it to legal rulings.
5
Identify the fifth condition: the branch case must not be explicitly covered by a text (mansus 'alayh).
If the branch is already ruled by nass, qiyas is either redundant (if in agreement) or contradictory (if in disagreement). The majority prohibit qiyas in both cases, but Samarkand scholars allow it for reinforcement.
This condition prevents unnecessary ijtihad where clear text suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل شروط صحة القياس
أي شروط صحة القياس. ١٢ أي القياس . ١٢
فصل شروط صحة القياس خمسة أحدها: أن لا يكون في مقابلة النص، والثاني: أن لا يتضمن تغيير حكم من أحكام النص، والثالث: أن لا يكون المعدى حكما لا يعقل معناه والرابع: أن يقع التعليل لحكم شرعي لا لأمر لغوي والخامس: أن لا يكون الفرع منصوصا عليه، ومثال فوات الشرط الأول
(١) قوله: [أحدها ... إلخ] أي: الأوّل أن لا يكون القياس الظيّ الذي له شبه من الراي معارضاً ومنافياً للنص الصحيح المعمول به كالآية وخبر الراوي الفقيه أو مطلقاً على ما حققنا، وكذا بإزاء قـــول الصحابي فما لا يدرك ،عندنا كذا في "الحصول". ١٢
(٢) قوله والثاني أن لا يتضمّن ... إلخ والمراد بالتغيير تغير المعنى المفهوم من النص لغة دون التغي الحاصل من الخصوص إلى العموم، فإنّه من ضروريات التعليق؛ إذ لا فائدة فيه إلا تعميم حكم النص، كذا في بعض الحواشي. ١٢
(٣) قوله: [تغيير حكم] أي: لا يتغير في الفرع حكم الأصل من إطلاقه أو تقييده أو غير ذلك ممـا يتعلّق بنفس الحكم، وإنما يقع باعتبار المحل وباعتبار صيرورته ظنّياً في الفرع، كذا في "التلويح". ١٢ (٤) قوله: [والثالث أن لا يكون المعدى حكماً... إلخ] أي: ثابتاً بأحد الأصول الثلاثة، وفيه إشارة إلى أنّ حكم الأصل لا يجوز أن يكون ثابتاً بالقياس؛ لأنه إن اتحدت العلة بالقياسين فذكر الواسطة ضائع، وإن لم يتحد بطل أحد القياسين لابتنائه على غير العلّة التي اعتبرها الشارع في الحكم، كذا قيل. ١٢ (٥) قوله والرابع أن يقع التعليل... إلخ الفرق بين التعليل والقياس بالاعتبار لا بالذات؛ لأنّ حكم مواضع النصوص إذا تعلل بعلة يسمى تعليلاً وإذا تعدّي الحكم من الأصل إلى الفرع وتقرر فيه يسمّى قياساً فيكون التعليل في الابتداء والقياس في الانتهاء، كذا في "المعدن". ١٢ (٦) قوله: [لحكم شرعي... إلخ لأن القياس حجّة شرعية فيتعرّف به الحكم الشرعي دون الحكم اللغوي؛ لأنّ الشيء إنما يعرف ما هو من بابه، ألا ترى أنّ الدلائل النحوية لايعرف بها أحكام الشرع فكـــــذا بالقياس الشرعي لا يعرف إلا ما كان حكماً شرعياً، وعن ابن شريح وجماعة من أصحاب الشافعي أنه يجوز إثبات الأسامي بالقياس اللغوي، ثُمّ يترتب عليه الأحكام وهو مذهب أهل العربية، والدليل على فساد هذا النوع من القياس يأتي في المتن ،فانتظره، كذا في "المعدن". ١٢ (۷) قوله: [والخامس أن لا يكون الفرع... إلخ] لأنّ التعدية إن كانت على وفاق النص الذي في الفـــــرع فلا فائدة فيه؛ لأن النص يغني عنه وإن كانت على خلافه فهو باطل لمناقضته حكم النص وهذا مختار عامة المشايخ، وأما مختار مشايخ "سمرقند" رحمهم الله أنه يجوز التعليل على موافقة النص وهو الأشبه؛ لأنّ فيه تأكيد النص على معنى أنه لولا النصّ لكان الحكم ثابتاً بالتعليل ولا مانع في الشرع والعقل عن تعاضد الأدلّة وتأكد بعضها ببعض، فإنّ الشرع قد ورد بآيات كثيرة وأحاديث متعدّدة في حكم واحد و ملأ السلف كتبهم بالتمسك بالنص، والمعقول في حكم ولم ينقل عن أحد نكير فكان إجماعاً علـــــى جوازه، هذا توضيح كلام "المعدن". ١٢
فهذا قياس في مقابلة النص وهو حديث الأعرابي الذي في عينـــه سوء، وكذلك إذا قلنا : «جاز حج المرأة مع المحرم فيجوز مع الأمينات كان هذا قياسا " بمقابلة النص وهو قوله عليه السلام: «لا يحل لإمرأة تؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر أن تسافر سفراً يكون ثلاثة أيام فصاعداً إلا مع ذي محرم».
(۱) قوله: [فهذا قياس في مقابلة النص لا يقال بل ينتقض الطهارة بالقذف قياساً على القهقهة لكونــــه أعظم جناية؛ لأنّ شرط القياس أن يكون المعدى حكماً يعقل معناه، وحديث القهقهة ورد غير معقول المعنى؛ لأنّ الانتقاض إنما يكون بخروج النجاسة والقهقهة ليست بنجاسة حتى ينتقض بها ولا يعقـــــل معنى الانتقاض بها، كذا في "المعدن". ١٢
(۲) قوله: [كان هذا قياسا ... آه] وجه المقابلة أنّ الشارع حرّم المسافرة على العموم واستثنى منه المسافرة مع الشيخين، فكان المسافرة مع غيرهما داخلة تحت التحريم على الإطلاق سواء كانت مع الرجل أو مع المرأة الأمينة ،وغيرها، وللخصم أن يقول: إنّ الأمينات ألحقت بها فكانت في معناهما ومثلـه لا يفيــــد مخالفة النص كما في قوله عليه السلام: «وإنّما الوضوء على من نام مضطجعاً» ألحقت صورة الاتكاء بالاضطجاع مع أن كلمة «إنما» للحصر. ١٢
(۳) قوله: [لا يحلّ... إلخ] رواه الطبراني عن أبي أمامة رفعه «لا يحل لامرأة مسلمة أن تحجّ إلا مع زوج أو ذي رحم محرم ورواه محمد في الآثار برواية أبي سعد وفي آخره «ولا تسافر المرأة إلا مع زوجها أو مع ذي رحم محرم منها» وهو قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله وقال مالك والشافعي رحمه الله : إذا خرجت في رفقة مأمونة جاز.
Chapter: Conditions for the validity of qiyas. The conditions for the validity of qiyas are five: First: that it does not oppose a textual proof (nass). Second: that it does not involve changing a ruling of the textual proofs. Third: that the transferred [ruling] is not a ruling whose meaning is not rationally comprehensible. Fourth: that the attribution of cause (ta'lil) is for a legal ruling, not for a linguistic matter. Fifth: that the branch case is not explicitly mentioned in the text. An example of the violation of the first condition: ... (followed by commentary and examples).
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a rule-statement from Usul al-Shashi, listing the five conditions for the validity of qiyas. The author, Nizam al-Din al-Shashi, enumerates them concisely. The commentary (Ahsan al-Hawashi) expands each condition. Condition one prevents qiyas from contradicting a clear scriptural text (nass). Condition two ensures qiyas does not alter the original ruling's essential meaning. Condition three requires the original ruling's underlying rationale ('illa) to be comprehensible, excluding purely devotional matters. Condition four restricts qiyas to legal rulings, not linguistic or grammatical ones. Condition five forbids qiyas on a branch already governed by nass, as it would be redundant or contradictory. The footnotes provide detailed discussions, including a dispute on whether qiyas may be used to reinforce a nass (Samarkand scholars allowing it). The example of qahqaha (laughter in prayer) versus qadhf (false accusation) illustrates condition one: qiyas cannot override a hadith that rules laughter nullifies wudu, even if qadhf seems graver, because the hadith's rationale is not analogizable. The women-traveling example shows qiyas being rejected when it contradicts a specific prophetic prohibition.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a branch case (far') due to shared effective cause ('illa).
النص (al-nass): A clear textual proof from Quran or Sunnah that explicitly states a ruling.
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause or rationale that justifies a legal ruling and is common to both original and branch cases.
التعليل (al-ta'lil): The act of identifying and stating the 'illa for a ruling; the initial step before qiyas proper.
الفرع (al-far'): The new case to which the ruling from the original case is extended through qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the five conditions for valid qiyas, which of the following best illustrates the first condition (that qiyas must not oppose nass)?
A) Qiyas that extends the prohibition of wine to narcotics based on intoxication.
B) Qiyas that requires wudu for laughter in prayer despite a hadith explicitly stating it nullifies wudu, arguing that a more serious sin (qadhf) does not nullify wudu.
C) Qiyas that permits traveling without a mahram because trustworthy women are similar to male guardians.
D) B and C both violate the first condition.

Key Takeaway
The five conditions for valid qiyas ensure that analogical reasoning does not contradict or replace clear divine texts; understanding them is essential for proper ijtihad.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Qiyas Muqabil al-Nass: Invalidity of Analogy Opposing Explicit Text
Explaining qiyas opposing nass with three examples and a scholarly dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify qiyas muqabil al-nass, apply the Hanafi rule that such qiyas is invalid, and evaluate the Samarqand position permitting ta'lil mawafiq al-nass.

Core Idea
Analogy that contradicts an explicit text is invalid; causal reasoning that confirms the text is permissible.

In Hanafi usul, qiyas is a valid source of law, but it cannot oppose an explicit nass. This lesson examines the concept of qiyas muqabil al-nass through three classic examples and explores the scholarly difference between the majority Hanafis and the Samarqand school regarding ta'lil that agrees with the nass.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition
Define qiyas muqabil al-nass and its legal status as invalid (bāṭil). Note that the 'opposition' means the analogy would overturn or restrict the clear ruling of the nass.
The nass must be explicit and applicable to the case.
2
Analyze the first two examples
Work through the examples: (1) loud laughter in prayer vs. accusing a chaste woman; (2) woman traveling with trustworthy women vs. with a mahram. Identify the nass and why the qiyas opposes it.
The hadith on travel is quoted: 'لا يحل لامرأة...'
3
Analyze the third example and the general rule
The third example involves changing an absolute (muṭlaq) ruling to a restricted (muqayyad) one via qiyas, e.g., requiring intention for wuḍū’ via qiyas on tayammum, or requiring purity for ṭawāf via qiyas on ṣalāh. This also constitutes qiyas muqabil al-nass.
Such analogies would change the explicit text.
4
Identify the dispute
Contrast the general Hanafi position (reject any qiyas with a nass) with the Samarqand position (permit ta'līl that agrees with the nass). Understand the evidence each side uses.
The Samarqand view is considered 'ashbah' (more appropriate) by the author.
5
Apply the rule to new scenarios
Given a hypothetical analogy, determine if it is muqabil al-nass or valid ta'līl mawāfiq.

فصل شروط صحة القياس القياس في مقابلة النص فيما حكي أن الحسن بن زياد سئل عن القهقهة في الصلاة فقال انتقضت الطهارة بها قال السائل لو قذف محصنة في الصلاة لا ينتقض به الوضوء مع أن قذف المحصنة أعظم جناية فكيف ينتقض بالقهقهة وهي دونه فهذا قياس في مقابلة النص وهو حديث الأعرابي الذي في عينه دون من القذف وكذلك إذا قلنا جاز حج المرأة مع المحرم فيجوز مع الأمينات كان هذا قياسا بمقابلة النص وهو قوله عليه السلام لا يحل لامرأة تؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر أن تسافر فوق ثلاثة أيام ولياليها إلا ومعها أبوها أو زوجها أو ذو رحم محرم منها عامة المشايخ وأما مختار مشايخ سمرقند رحمهم الله أنه يجوز التعليل على موافقة النص وهو الأشبه لأن فيه تأكيد النص على معنى أنه لولا النص لكان الحكم ثابتا بالتعليل ولا مانع في الشرع والعقل عن تعاضد الأدلة وتأكد بعضها ببعض فإن الشرع قد ورد بآيات كثيرة وأحاديث متعددة في حكم واحد وملأ السلف كتبهم بالتمسك بالنص والمعقول في حكم ولم ينقل عن أحد نكير فكان إجماعا على جوازه هذا توضيح كلام المعدن ومثال الثاني وهو ما يتضمن تغيير حكم من أحكام النص ما يقال النية شرط في الوضوء بالقياس على التيمم فإن هذا يوجب تغيير آية الوضوء من الإطلاق إلى التقييد وكذلك إذا قلنا الطواف بالبيت صلاة بالخبر فيشترط له الطهارة وستر العورة كالصلاة كان هذا قياسا يوجب تغيير نص الطواف من الإطلاق إلى القيد ومثال الثالث قول الشوافع
Chapter: Conditions for the validity of analogy. Analogy in opposition to the text: It is narrated that al-Hasan ibn Ziyad was asked about loud laughter in prayer, and he said: 'Purity is nullified by it.' The questioner said: 'If a man accuses a chaste woman [of adultery] in prayer, wudu is not nullified by it, even though accusing a chaste woman is a greater sin, so how can it be nullified by laughter while it is lesser?' This is an analogy in opposition to the text, and it is the hadith of the Bedouin whose eye was less than [the crime of] accusation. Similarly, if we say: 'A woman may perform Hajj with a mahram, so she may also perform it with trustworthy women,' this is an analogy in opposition to the text, namely his statement, peace be upon him: 'It is not lawful for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day to travel more than three days except with her father, husband, or a male mahram.' The general [opinion] of the mashayikh [is that this is invalid], but the chosen position of the mashayikh of Samarqand, may Allah have mercy on them, is that it is permissible to base the legal cause [ta'lil] in agreement with the text, and this is more appropriate, because it involves confirmation of the text in the sense that, were it not for the text, the ruling would be established by the legal cause, and there is no impediment in the Sharia or reason against the mutual support of evidences and the strengthening of some by others. Indeed, the Sharia has come with many verses and numerous hadith on a single ruling, and the Salaf filled their books with adherence to the text and the rational [approach] in rulings, and no one has transmitted a denial, so it is a consensus on its permissibility. This is an explanation of the words of al-Ma'dan. The second example: that which involves changing a ruling from the rulings of the text is what is said: 'Intention is a condition for wudu' by analogy on tayammum. This entails changing the verse of wudu from absolute to restricted. Similarly, if we say: 'Circumambulation of the House is prayer according to the report, so it requires purity and covering of the private parts like prayer,' this is an analogy that entails changing the text of circumambulation from absolute to restricted. The third example: the statement of the Shafi'is.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on conditions for the validity of qiyas (analogical reasoning) discusses a key usul principle: qiyas that directly opposes an explicit textual ruling (nass) is invalid. The author presents three examples to illustrate this. First, the case of loud laughter in prayer nullifying wudu (a ruling established by hadith) versus accusing a chaste woman, which is a greater sin but does not nullify wudu. Attempting to draw an analogy from the greater to the lesser would oppose the nass. Second, the prohibition of a woman traveling without a mahram; permitting her to travel with trustworthy women would analogize to the permissibility with a mahram, but this contradicts the explicit hadith. Third, the requirement of intention for wudu by analogy on tayammum, and the requirement of ritual purity for tawaf by analogy on prayer, both would restrict an absolute command and thus invalidly change the nass. The text then notes a scholarly dispute: the general mashayikh reject such qiyas, but the Samarqand school permits ta'lil (causal reasoning) in agreement with the nass, as it reinforces rather than contradicts the text. They argue that multiple evidences can support a single ruling, and this practice is effectively accepted by consensus among the Salaf. The passage contrasts these positions, showing that while qiyas muqabil al-nass is generally prohibited, there is nuance regarding ta'lil mawafiq al-nass.

Key Terms
القياس في مقابلة النص (al-qiyās fī muqābalat al-naṣṣ): An analogical reasoning that directly opposes an explicit textual ruling; such qiyas is invalid in Hanafi usul.
التعليل على موافقة النص (al-ta‘līl ‘alā mawāfaqat al-naṣṣ): Causal reasoning that confirms and reinforces the ruling of the nass rather than opposing it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of qiyas muqabil al-nass according to the passage?
A) Qiyas that establishes a new ruling not mentioned in the text
B) Qiyas that derives the prohibition of wine from the prohibition of khamr
C) Qiyas that permits women to travel with trustworthy women based on the permissibility with a mahram
D) Qiyas that is based on an explicit ‘illa from the text

Key Takeaway
Qiyas that directly contradicts an explicit nass is invalid; ta‘līl that confirms the nass is permissible according to some Hanafis.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Conditions for Valid Qiyas in Hanafi Usul
Explanation of conditions for valid qiyas with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for valid qiyas according to the Hanafi school and apply them to evaluate whether a proposed qiyas is valid.

Core Idea
Qiyas is invalid if it changes a clear text or extends a ruling whose rationale is not understood.

In this passage from al-Shashi's Usul al-Fiqh, the author explains the conditions that must be met for analogical reasoning (qiyas) to be valid within the Hanafi school. The Hanafis restrict qiyas in two critical ways: it must not alter a clear scriptural text (nass), and the original ruling must be rationally comprehensible (ma'qul al-ma'na). Through several illustrative examples, the passage demonstrates the consequences of violating these conditions, distinguishing permissible analogy from invalid extensions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Core Conditions
Read the passage carefully and extract the two main conditions for valid qiyas. The first is that qiyas must not change a clear text (nass). The second is that the original ruling (al-asl) must be ma'qul al-ma'na—i.e., its effective cause ('illah) is rationally understood.
These conditions are foundational for evaluating any analogy.
2
Analyze the First Condition: Qiyas Must Not Change a Nass
Consider the examples: requiring intention (niyyah) for wudu by analogy to tayammum, and requiring purity for tawaf by analogy to prayer. Both would change an absolute command into a conditional one, which is invalid because qiyas cannot override a clear text.
The nass in wudu is the verse without mention of intention; in tawaf it is the absolute command to circumambulate.
3
Analyze the Second Condition: Original Ruling Must Be Ma'qul al-Ma'na
Examine the examples of wudu with nabidh (date-water) and building upon prayer after a hadath. The original rulings are established by text contrary to analogy (khilaf al-qiyas) and have no rationally understood 'illah. Therefore, they cannot be extended to other cases.
Nabidh is a dispensation; the ruling on building upon prayer is based on textual indication (dalalah), not qiyas.
4
Evaluate the Shafi'i Argument about Two Qullahs
The Shafi'is argue that if two qullahs of najis water combine, they become pure by analogy to a single qullah becoming pure when a small impurity falls in it. The Hanafis reject this because the original ruling (if established) is not rationally understood and the hadith is weak.
This illustrates how the second condition blocks invalid analogies even when a common 'illah might be claimed.
5
Summarize the Epistemological Rationale
Qiyas is a tool for extending understood 'illah from a known case to a new case. It cannot create new rulings that contradict texts, nor can it replicate divine commands that are purely ta'abbudi. This preserves the authority of revelation.
Hanafis prioritize textual certainty over analogical reasoning.

Chapter on conditions for the validity of qiyas. ... (full literal translation would be lengthy and incomplete due to OCR issues) ... The passage discusses examples of invalid qiyas: changing a divine text, and qiyas on rulings established contrary to analogy.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage from al-Shashi's Usul discusses the conditions for the validity of qiyas (analogical reasoning). The author presents examples of invalid qiyas: (1) qiyas that changes a clear text (nass), such as requiring intention for wudu by analogy with tayammum, which would change the absolute command of wudu to a conditional one; (2) qiyas that adds conditions to tawaf by analogy with prayer, changing its absolute permission; (3) qiyas on rulings that are themselves established contrary to analogy (thabit bi khilaf al-qiyas), like the permissibility of wudu with nabidh (date-water) which is a dispensation, so it cannot be extended to other drinks; (4) qiyas on rulings whose 'illah (ratio legis) is not rationally understood, such as the ruling of building upon prayer after a hadath, which is known by textual indication (dalalah) not qiyas; and (5) the Shafi'i argument about two qullahs of water becoming pure when combined, which the Hanafis reject because the original ruling (if established) is not rationally understood and the hadith is weak. The commentary elaborates these points with additional rulings and refutations.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: deriving a ruling for a new case from an original case due to a shared effective cause ('illah).
النص (al-nass): A clear scriptural text (Qur'an or hadith) that is unambiguous.
ما لا يعقل معناه (ma la ya'qilu ma'anahu): A ruling whose rationale is not rationally comprehensible, known only through divine command (ta'abbudi).
خلاف القياس (khilaf al-qiyas): A ruling established by text that is contrary to general legal principles (e.g., a dispensation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis reject qiyas on the permissibility of wudu with nabidh (date-water) to other types of nabidh?
A) Because nabidh is not a valid analogy.
B) Because the original ruling for wudu with date-water is established by text contrary to analogy, so it cannot be extended.
C) Because date-water is pure water.
D) Because qiyas is not allowed in matters of worship.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a powerful but bounded tool: it must never alter a clear text, and it cannot extend rulings whose rationale is beyond human comprehension.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
6 min
The Condition of Ma'qul al-Ma'na in Qiyas
Stating a condition for qiyas: the ruling in the original must be rationally intelligible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a ruling is ma'qul al-ma'na and determine whether qiyas can be applied, using the Hanafi criteria.

Core Idea
A ruling established contrary to analogy cannot be extended by qiyas because its rationale is unknown.

Qiyas is valid only when the ruling in the original case is rationally understood (ma'qul al-ma'na). This lesson explains why rulings that come as exceptions to general principles are restricted to their specific texts. The classic example is building prayer after hadath—a textual ruling that contradicts the general qiyas that hadath invalidates prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for qiyas
The passage states that qiyas requires the original ruling to be ma'qul al-ma'na (rationally intelligible). First, locate this condition in the text.
The condition is in the first sentence: 'لا يصح أن يعدى الحكم … إلا إذا كان الحكم في الأصل معقول المعنى'.
2
Understand the example: building prayer after hadath
The example is a specific ruling: if a person experiences hadath (e.g., vomiting or nosebleed) during prayer, they may leave, perform wudu, and continue from where they left off. This is established by hadith.
This ruling is an exception because generally hadath invalidates prayer. It is 'khilaf al-qiyas' (contrary to analogy).
3
Analyze why the ruling is not ma'qul al-ma'na
Since the ruling contradicts the general principle that hadath nullifies prayer, its underlying rationale (illah) is not rationally comprehensible. The illah of the general qiyas is the corrupting effect of hadath, but the text overrides it without a clear ratio legis.
Hanafis argue that if a ruling is contrary to qiyas, its meaning is not understood ('لم يعقل معناه'), so it cannot serve as an asl for further qiyas.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that qiyas is permissible even on such rulings because the mujtahid can identify an illah through ijtihad. The passage rebuts this by stating that the illah is unknown.
This dispute has practical consequences (thamarah): for similar events like a cut, Hanafis do not allow building prayer, while Shafi'is do via qiyas.
5
Apply the rule to a new case
Test your understanding: is the ruling on building prayer after a nosebleed applicable to a person who faints? According to Hanafis, no—because the original ruling is text-specific and cannot be extended.
This step internalizes the distinction between rulings that are ma'qul al-ma'na and those that are not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل شروط صحة القياس لا يصح أن يعدى الحكم من الأصل إلى الفرع إلا إذا كان الحكم في الأصل معقول المعنى. ومثال ذلك: البناء على الصلاة في الحدث ثابت بالنص على خلاف القياس؛ لأن الحدث ينافي الصلاة، فلا يقاس عليه غيره. وقال الشافعي رحمه الله: يجوز. ولنا أن الحكم إذا كان ثابتاً بخلاف القياس لم يعقل معناه، فاستحال تعديته إلى الفرع.
Chapter: Conditions for the validity of qiyas. It is not permissible to transfer the ruling from the original to the branch unless the ruling in the original is intelligible in meaning. An example of that: building upon prayer in the case of hadath is established by the text contrary to analogy, because hadath contradicts prayer, so other things are not measured upon it. Al-Shafi'i said: it is permissible. For us: when the ruling is established contrary to analogy, its meaning is not understood, so it is impossible to extend it to the branch.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage states a fundamental condition for qiyas: the hukm (ruling) in the original case must be rationally understood (ma'qul al-ma'na) so that it can be extended to a new case. The example given is the ruling that a person who experiences hadath (e.g., vomiting or nosebleed) during prayer may build upon his previous prayer after performing wudu. This ruling is established by a specific hadith ("Whoever vomits or has a nosebleed in his prayer, let him leave and do wudu and build upon his prayer") and is contrary to analogy (qiyas) because hadath invalidates prayer in general. Since the original ruling is not rationally understood (its rationale is not fully grasped), it cannot be extended via qiyas to other similar events. The Hanafi position is that such rulings are restricted to their specific textual occurrences. Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed, allowing qiyas even on rulings that are contrary to analogy. The teacher clarifies that the Hanafi view is based on the principle that what is established contrary to analogy cannot be used as a basis for further analogical extension.

Key Terms
معقول المعنى (ma'qul al-ma'na): The ruling's rationale is rationally understandable, allowing its 'illa to be identified and extended via qiyas.
خلاف القياس (khilaf al-qiyas): A ruling that contradicts what would be expected from general analogical reasoning; such rulings are typically limited to their textual basis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can the ruling on building prayer after hadath be extended via qiyas to a person who faints in prayer?
A) Yes, because the cause is the same — loss of wudu.
B) No, because the original ruling is contrary to analogy and is limited to its textual cases.
C) Yes, because all rulings can be extended by qiyas.
D) No, because fainting is different from hadath in a significant way.

Key Takeaway
A ruling that is contrary to analogy (khilaf al-qiyas) is not ma'qul al-ma'na, and therefore cannot be used as an asl for qiyas; it is restricted to its specific textual occurrence.
