Deriving 'Illah from Sunnah and Ijma in Qiyas
Illustrates how 'illah is derived from hadith and ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the 'illah from a primary text (Sunnah or Ijma) and apply it to analogous cases via qiyas.

Core Idea
The 'illah in qiyas can be derived from explicit hadith or consensus, then extended to new cases sharing the same cause.

In this passage from Usul al-Shashi, we see practical examples of how the 'illah (legal cause) for qiyas is identified from the Sunnah and from Ijma. You will learn to spot the explicit attribute designated as the cause and understand how it transfers the ruling to new cases. This is essential training for usul reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the source of the 'illah
The passage gives three examples: two from the Prophet's sayings (Sunnah) and one from scholarly consensus (Ijma). Identify which source each example relies on.
Sunnah examples: sleep hadith and istihadah hadith. Ijma example: minority for guardianship.
2
Identify the textually designated 'illah
In each example, the text explicitly mentions the attribute that causes the ruling. For sleep, it is 'relaxation of joints' (istirkha' al-mafasil). For istihadah, it is 'bursting of blood' (infijar al-dam). For guardianship, it is 'minority' (sughr).
The 'illah is often introduced by a phrase like 'because' or 'for when'.
3
Note the original ruling (hukm al-asl)
Each 'illah is attached to a specific ruling. Sleep lying down requires wudu; istihadah requires wudu and prayer; minority gives the father guardianship.
The ruling is the legal consequence attached to the asl.
4
Extract the commonality (jami')
The 'illah is the common attribute that connects the original case to the new cases. For sleep, it is relaxation; for istihadah, it is blood bursting; for guardianship, it is minority.
The jami' is the shared attribute that justifies extending the ruling.
5
Apply the 'illah to new cases
The text shows the far' (new case) that shares the 'illah. Leaning sleep, fainting, and intoxication share relaxation. Phlebotomy and cupping share blood bursting. No new cases are given for minority, but the principle stands.
The ruling from the asl transfers to the far' because the 'illah is present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل القياس الشرعي
ومثال العلة المعلومة بالسنة في قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: ليس الوضوء على من نام قائما أو قاعدا أو راكعا أو ساجدا إنما الوضوء على من نام مضطجعا فإنه إذا نام مضطجعا استرخت مفاصله. جعل استرخاء المفاصل علة فيتعدى الحكم بهذه العلة إلى النوم مستنداً أو متكئاً إلى شيء لو أزيل عنه لسقط، وكذلك يتعدى الحكم بهذه العلة إلى الإغماء والسكر والجامع وجود الاسترخاء في الكل. ومثال العلة المعلومة بالسنة أيضاً قوله عليه السلام: توضئي وصلي وإن قطر الدم على الحصير قطرا فإنه دم عرق انفجر. جعل انفجار الدم علة فتعدى الحكم بهذه العلة إلى الفصد والحجامة والجامع انفجار الدم في كل منها. ومثال العلة المعلومة بالإجماع: وهو ولاية الأب. بالإجماع فيما قلنا: الصغر علة لولاية الأب في حق الصغير فيثبت الحكم.
Chapter on Legal Analogy (Qiyas). An example of the cause known from the Sunnah is in his saying, peace be upon him: 'Wudu is not required for one who slept standing, sitting, bowing, or prostrating; wudu is only required for one who slept lying down, for when he sleeps lying down his joints relax.' He made the relaxation of joints a cause, so the ruling extends by this cause to sleeping while leaning or reclining on something such that if it were removed he would fall, and likewise the ruling extends by this cause to fainting and intoxication, and the commonality is the existence of relaxation in all. Also an example of the cause known from the Sunnah is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Perform wudu and pray, and if blood drips on a straw mat, drop by drop, it is blood from a burst vein.' He made the bursting of blood a cause, so the ruling extends by this cause to phlebotomy and cupping, and the commonality is the bursting of blood in each. An example of the cause known by consensus: the guardianship of the father. By consensus in what we said: minority is a cause for the father's guardianship over the minor, so the ruling is established.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi explains the different sources for identifying the 'illah (legal cause) used in qiyas. The first 'illah is derived from an explicit hadith: the Prophet (SAW) stated that wudu is only required for sleep in a lying-down position because it causes relaxation of the joints. This relaxation is the 'illah, and the ruling extends to any sleep where the person leans on something such that if removed, he would fall. It further extends to fainting and intoxication because they involve an even greater loss of body control, thus the relaxation is more pronounced. The commonality (jami') is the presence of relaxation. The second 'illah is from the hadith of Fatimah bint Abi Hubaysh: the Prophet (SAW) instructed her to do wudu for each prayer and said that the blood from istihadah is from a burst vein. The 'illah is the bursting of the blood vessel, so the ruling (wudu required due to impurity) extends to phlebotomy and cupping. The third 'illah is derived from consensus (ijma'): minority is the cause for the father's guardianship over his child. This is accepted by all scholars. The passage demonstrates how qiyas operates: identify the 'illah from a source text, then apply it to analogous cases.

Key Terms
العلة (al-'illah): The effective attribute or legal cause that is identified from the primary text and used to extend the ruling to new cases via qiyas.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning that applies a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared legal cause ('illah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi example of qiyas from the Sunnah, what is the 'illah for wudu after sleep?
A) The act of sleeping itself
B) The relaxation of joints when lying down
C) The duration of sleep
D) The position of the body during sleep

Key Takeaway
The 'illah for qiyas can be explicitly derived from the Sunnah or from Ijma, and it is the common attribute that justifies extending a ruling to new cases.

The ‘Illa and Two Types of Qiyas
Defines ‘illa and two types of qiyas with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the ‘illa in a given qiyas and distinguish between qiyas where the transferred ruling is of the same type versus the same kind.

Core Idea
The ‘illa is the essential link that transfers a ruling from an original case to a new one; its discovery may be from text, consensus, or appropriateness.

Legal analogy (qiyas) is a cornerstone of Hanafi jurisprudence, but it is not arbitrary — it requires a precise cause (‘illa) that justifies extending a ruling. This lesson unpacks the ‘illa through concrete examples from the hadith of istihadah and the consensus on father’s guardianship. You will also learn the two categories of qiyas: when the transferred ruling is exactly the same type as the original, and when it is merely of the same kind. Mastery of these tools is essential for sound istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ‘illa in a given analogy
Look for the common attribute that the jurist explicitly or implicitly uses to connect the original case (asl) to the new case (far‘). In the passage, the Prophet identifies 'bursting of a blood vessel' as the cause for nullifying wudu in istihadah.
The ‘illa must be appropriate (munasib) and not overridden by a stronger evidence.
2
Trace the qiyas chain from the hadith example
Asl = case of istihadah, hukm asl = wudu nullified, ‘illa = bursting of blood, far‘ = phlebotomy/cupping, hukm far‘ = wudu nullified. This illustrates how the same ‘illa extends the ruling.
The hadith itself provides the ‘illa explicitly (ta‘lil), making the qiyas strong.
3
Trace the qiyas chain from the consensus example
Asl = minor son, hukm asl = father’s guardianship in marriage, ‘illa = minority (sighar), far‘ = minor daughter, hukm far‘ = same guardianship. The ‘illa is established by consensus (ijma‘) according to the author.
Here the ‘illa is not from text but from collective agreement of scholars.
4
Distinguish the two types of qiyas
The passage states that qiyas is of two types: (1) the transferred ruling is the same type (naw‘) as the original ruling, e.g., guardianship in marriage for a boy and for a girl are both 'guardianship in marriage'; (2) the transferred ruling is of the same kind (jins) but not identical, e.g., guardianship of property is of the same 'genre' but a different specific ruling.
This classification affects how strictly the analogy is applied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل القياس الشرعي العلة إلى الإغماء والسكر ، وكذلك قوله عليه السلام: «توضئي ، وصلي، وإن قطر الدم على الحصير قطرا فإنّه دم عرق انفجر» جعل انفجار الدم علة فتعدّى الحكم بهذه العلة الى الفصد والحجامة ومثال العلة المعلومة بالإجماع: وهو ولاية الأب بالإجماع فيما قلنا: الصغر علّة لولاية الأب في حق الصغير فيثبت الحكم في حق الصغيرة لوجود العلّة، والبلوغ عن عقل علّة لزوال ولاية الأب في حق الغلام فيتعدّى الحكم إلى الجارية بهذه العلة، وانفجار الدم علّة الإنتقاض للطهارة في حق المستحاضة فيتعدّى الحكم الى غيرها لوجود العلة، ثم بعد ذلك نقول: القياس على نوعين أحدهما: أن يكون الحكم المعدى من نوع الحكم الثابت في الأصل، والثاني: أن يكون من جنسه، مثال الاتحاد في النوع ما قلنا: إن الصغر علة لولاية الإنكاح في حق الغلام فيثبت ولاية الإنكاح في حق الجارية لوجود العلة.
Chapter on legal analogy: The cause extends to fainting and intoxication, and likewise his saying, peace be upon him: 'Perform ablution, pray, and if blood drips on the mat, it is a vein that burst.' He made the bursting of blood a cause, so the ruling extends by this cause to phlebotomy and cupping. And an example of the cause known by consensus: it is the guardianship of the father. By consensus, according to what we said: minority is a cause for the father's guardianship over the minor, so the ruling is established for the minor girl because of the existence of the cause. And puberty with reason is a cause for removal of the father's guardianship over the boy, so the ruling extends to the girl by this cause. And the bursting of blood is a cause for nullification of purity for the woman with chronic bleeding, so the ruling extends to others due to the existence of the cause. Then after that we say: Qiyas is of two types: one where the transferred ruling is of the same type as the ruling established in the original; the second where it is of its kind. An example of unity in type is what we said: minority is a cause for guardianship of marriage over the boy, so guardianship of marriage is established over the girl due to the existence of the cause.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Usul al-Shashi explains the concept of the 'illa (legal cause) in qiyas and the two types of qiyas. The author first provides examples of 'illa from hadith: the Prophet's statement about istihadah (chronic bleeding) where the bursting of a blood vessel is identified as the cause for the obligation of ablution, and then analogically extends the ruling to phlebotomy and cupping. Next, an example of 'illa known by consensus is given: minority (sighar) is the cause for the father's guardianship over his minor son, and the same ruling applies to the minor daughter; conversely, puberty with reason causes the removal of that guardianship for the son, and this extends to the daughter. The same 'illa of bursting blood is then applied to the case of mustahadah (woman with chronic bleeding) to establish the nullification of purity, and the ruling extends to other cases. Finally, the author introduces the two types of qiyas: (1) where the ruling transferred is of the same type as the original (ittihad fi al-naw'), e.g., guardianship of marriage for a boy is the same type as for a girl; and (2) where it is of the same kind (ittihad fi al-jins), which is explained in the margin as sharing a common attribute while differing in another aspect, such as guardianship of property. The passage emphasizes that the 'illa must be a common attribute that justifies the extension of the ruling from the original case (asl) to the new case (far').

Key Terms
علة ('illa): A common attribute that is the basis for extending a ruling from the original case to a new case in qiyas.
قياس (qiyas): Extending a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a shared 'illa.
صغر (sighar): Minority or being underage, which is an 'illa for guardianship by the father.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Puberty
B) Minority (sighar)
C) Virginity
D) Bursting of blood

Key Takeaway
The 'illa is the linchpin of qiyas; it can be extracted from text, consensus, or appropriateness, and qiyas is either unity in type or unity in kind.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Two Types of Qiyas: Unity in Type and Unity in Genus
Defines and illustrates two types of legal analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qiyas with unity in type and unity in genus, and apply the Hanafi classification to legal examples involving a shared cause.

Core Idea
Legal analogy transfers either the exact ruling or a ruling of the same genus, based on a shared cause.

In this lesson from Usul al-Shashi, the author defines two distinct types of legal analogy (qiyas) that are fundamental to Hanafi istinbat. Using vivid examples from marriage guardianship and ritual purity, you will learn how jurists extend rulings when the cause (illa) is shared. The passage also introduces a famous dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i on the cause for guardianship over women, illustrating how understanding qiyas types shapes divergent rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
The author defines unity in type (al-ittihad fi al-naw') and unity in genus (al-ittihad fi al-jins). Understand the distinction: type means the transferred ruling is exactly the same; genus means it belongs to the same category of rulings.
The examples in the text illustrate each type clearly.
2
Examine the examples of unity in type
Study the two examples: (1) minority as cause for guardianship in marriage for both boys and girls, and (2) frequent coming and going (tawwaf) as cause for dropping impurity ruling for cat's leftover water and other household pets. In each, the transferred ruling is identical.
Notice that the cause (illa) is the same and the ruling is exactly the same type (e.g., guardianship or purity).
3
Examine the example of unity in genus
The example of frequent coming and going dropping the hardship of seeking permission for slaves, and also dropping the hardship of impurity of leftover water. Both are 'hardships' but of different kinds (permission vs. impurity). The ruling is of the same genus (removing hardship) but not identical in type.
This shows how the same cause can produce rulings that are similar in category but not identical.
4
Analyze the dispute
The passage raises a third issue: Is the cause for guardianship over a woman minority or virginity? Hanafi says minority; Shafi'i says virginity. The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: a virgin girl whose father married her without consent was given a choice by the Prophet. This shows that virginity does not remove her right to consent, so the cause must be minority.
The dispute impacts the ruling for adult virgin women: Hanafi allows her to choose her own husband, while Shafi'i holds that her father can marry her without her consent.
5
Apply the classification
Given a new case with a shared cause, determine whether the transferred ruling is of the same type or same genus. This requires analyzing the nature of the ruling and its category.
Use the examples in this lesson as models.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل القياس الشرعي ثم بعد ذلك نقول : القياس على نوعين أحدهما: أن يكون الحكم المعدى من نوع الحكم الثابت في الأصل، والثاني: أن يكون من جنسه، مثال الاتحاد في النوع ما قلنا: إن الصغر علة لولاية الإنكاح في حق الغلام فيثبت ولاية الإنكاح في حق الجارية لوجود العلة فيها، وبه يثبت الحكم في الثيب الصغيرة، وكذلك قلنا: الطواف علة سقوط نجاسة السؤر في سؤر الهرة فيتعدى الحكم الى سؤر سواكن البيوت لوجود العلة، وبلوغ الغلام عن عقل علة زوال ولاية الإنكاح فيزول الولاية عن الجارية بحكم هذه العلة، ومثال الاتحاد في الجنس ما يقال كثرة الطواف علة سقوط حرج الاستئذان في حق ما ملكت أيماننا فيسقط حرج نجاسة السؤر بهذه العلة فإن هذا الحرج من جنس ذلك الحرج، ونسأل عن المسئلة الثالثة أن علّة الولاية على المرأة في النكاح هل هي الصغر كما في الغلام أو البكارة، فاخترنا الأول، واختار الشافعي رحمه الله الثاني
Chapter: Legal Analogy. Then after that we say: Qiyas is of two types: one where the transferred ruling is of the same type as the ruling established in the original, and the second where it is of its genus. An example of unity in type is what we said: minority is the cause for guardianship of marriage in the case of a boy, so guardianship of marriage is established in the case of a girl due to the existence of the cause in her, and by it the ruling is established for a minor non-virgin. Similarly, we said: frequent coming and going is a cause for dropping the impurity of the leftover water in the leftover water of a cat, so the ruling transfers to the leftover water of household animals due to the existence of the cause. And the puberty of a boy with intellect is a cause for the removal of guardianship of marriage, so guardianship is removed from the girl by this ruling. An example of unity in genus is what is said: frequent coming and going is a cause for dropping the hardship of seeking permission in the case of those whom our right hands possess, so the hardship of impurity of leftover water drops by this cause, for this hardship is of the genus of that hardship. And we ask about the third issue: Is the cause for guardianship over a woman in marriage minority as in the boy, or virginity? We chose the former, and al-Shafi'i chose the latter.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi explains the two types of qiyas (legal analogy) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The first type is 'unity in type' where the ruling transferred is exactly the same ruling as in the original case. The second is 'unity in genus' where the ruling transferred belongs to the same category but is not identical. Examples: For unity in type, the cause of minority (sughr) establishes guardianship of marriage in both a young boy and a young girl. Similarly, the cause of frequent coming and going (tawwaf) drops the impurity ruling for the leftover water of cats and household animals. For unity in genus, the frequent coming and going drops the hardship of seeking permission for slaves, and by the same cause, the hardship of impurity of leftover water drops—both are hardships but of different types. The passage then addresses a dispute with Shafi'i: Hanafi holds that minority is the cause for guardianship in females, not virginity, supported by the hadith of Ibn Abbas about a virgin girl whose father married her and the Prophet gave her a choice.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Legal analogy: transferring a ruling from an original case to a branch case due to a shared cause (illa)
الاتحاد في النوع (al-ittihad fi al-naw'): Unity in type: the transferred ruling is exactly the same ruling as in the original
الاتحاد في الجنس (al-ittihad fi al-jins): Unity in genus: the transferred ruling is of the same category but not identical
العلة (al-illa): The effective cause that justifies the ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Unity in type uses a different cause; unity in genus uses the same cause.
C) Unity in type applies only to worship; unity in genus applies to transactions.
D) Unity in type is based on explicit text; unity in genus is based on reason.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas operates either by transferring an identical ruling (unity in type) or a ruling of the same genus, and the classification depends on the nature of the ruling, not the illa.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Types of Qiyas: Unity in Type vs. Genus
Explains two types of qiyas with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qiyas with unity in type and qiyas with unity in genus, and apply the Hanafi principle of tajnis al-illa to extend rulings.

Core Idea
Analogies transfer rulings when the cause shares a genus, even if species differ.

This passage from al-Shashi's Usul explains two modes of legal analogy: one where the cause is identical in type (naw'), and another where the cause shares a common genus (jins). Through examples from marriage guardianship and impurity rulings, it shows how the Hanafi school extends rulings using a broadened cause (tajnis al-illa). Understanding this distinction is key to mastering Hanafi qiyas methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
Look for the keywords 'al-ittihad fi al-naw'' (unity in type) and 'al-ittihad fi al-jins' (unity in genus). The first type requires the cause ('illa) to be exactly the same species; the second only requires it to belong to the same genus.
The passage labels these explicitly in the commentary.
2
Trace the example for unity in type
The cause of minority (sighar) establishes guardianship of marriage over a minor girl, even if she is a non-virgin (thayyib). The cause (minority) is exactly the same type as in the original case.
This refutes the Shafi'i view that virginity is the cause.
3
Trace the example for unity in genus
Frequent tawaf (circumambulation) is the cause for dropping the hardship of impurity in a cat's leftover. The same cause (frequent tawaf) also drops the hardship of seeking permission for slaves, because both hardships belong to the genus of 'hardship' (haraj).
The cause is not exactly the same species; it is a genus common to both.
4
Understand tajnis al-illa
Generalizing the cause to a broader meaning (jins) allows it to apply to multiple species. For example, the cause of 'inability to manage affairs' applies to both property and personal matters, establishing guardianship over both.
This is a distinct Hanafi methodology for extending rulings beyond the text.
5
Observe the madhhab dispute
The Shafi'i school uses virginity as the cause for guardianship over a minor girl, but the Hanafi school uses minority because it is common to both virgin and non-virgin. The practical difference: Hanafi allows guardianship over a thayyib minor; Shafi'i may not.
This dispute shows how cause identification affects rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أصول الشاشي مع أحسن الحواشي بالقياس. ١٢ فصل القياس الشرعي أي الصغر وهذه الواحد من نوع تلك الولاية. ١٢ أي ولاية النكاح. ١٢ الإنكاح في حق الجارية لوجود العلة فيها وبه يثبت الحكم في الثيب أي الصغر. ١٢ أي مثل الاتحاد في النوع في ما ذكرنا. ١٢ الصغيرة، وكذلك قلنا: الطوّاف علّة سقوط نجاسة السور في سؤر الهرة ١٢ عطف على قوله الصغر. ١٢ وهو سقوط نجاسة السور. ١٢ أي هوام الأرض من سكت زواياه. ۱۲ أي الطواف. ۱۲ فيتعدّى الحكم الى سؤر سواكن البيوت لوجود العلة ، وبلوغ الغلام عن عقل علة عن الغلام. ١٢ الغير البالغة. ١٢ أي البلوغ مع العقل. ١٢ زوال ولاية الإنكاح فيزول الولاية عن الجارية بحكم هذه العلة، ومثال أي اتحاد الحكم المعدى. ١٢ والكثرة ماخوذ عن صيغة المبالغة في قوله طوافون. ١٢ أي طلب الإذن عند الدخول. ١٢ الاتحاد في الجنس ما يقال كثرة الطوّاف علة سقوط حرج الاستئذان في أي المماليك. ١٢ أي سؤر الهرة وسواكن الحرج، كذا في "الشرح". ١٢ مجلس: "المدينة العلمية" (الدعوة الإسلامية) -( YEA )—  أصول الشاشي مع أحسن الحواشي . لأن حرج النجاسة غير حرج الاستيذان. ١٢ أي حرج الاستيذان. ١٢ الله فصل القياس الشرعي في الجارية. ١٢ من جنس ذلك الحرج لا من نوعه ، وكذلك الصغر علة ولاية التصرّف أي مثل الطواف. ١٢ أي مال الجارية. ١٢ للأب. ١٢ أي نفس الجارية. ١٢ وهي الصغر وهذه الولاية من جنس تلك الولاية لا من توعها. ۱۲ للأب Principles of al-Shashi with Ahsan al-Hawashi: By analogy. Section: Legal analogy. i.e., minority (sighar), and this one is a type of that guardianship. i.e., guardianship of marriage. The marriage contract regarding the girl due to the presence of the cause, and by it the ruling is established for the non-virgin, i.e., minority. i.e., like unity in type in what we mentioned. The young girl, and similarly we said: frequent tawaf (circumambulation) is the cause for the drop of impurity of the leftover (su'r) in the leftover of the cat. It is appended to his saying 'minority'. And it is the drop of impurity of the leftover. i.e., the insects of the earth whose corners are silent. i.e., the tawaf. So the ruling transfers to the leftover of domestic animals due to the presence of the cause. And the puberty of the boy with intellect is a cause regarding the boy. The non-major girl. i.e., puberty with intellect. The removal of guardianship of marriage, so guardianship is removed from the girl by the ruling of this cause. And the example of unity in genus: it is said that frequent tawaf is the cause for the removal of hardship of seeking permission regarding slaves. i.e., the leftover of the cat and domestic animals. i.e., hardship of the leftover. i.e., the right of what our right hands possess, so the hardship of impurity of the leftover drops due to this cause, for this hardship is frequent tawaf. (Then multiple footnotes explaining details).
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage explains two types of qiyas (analogy) in Hanafi usul: qiyas where the cause ('illa) is of the same type (naw') and qiyas where the cause is of the same genus (jins). The example for the first type: the cause of minority (sighar) establishes the guardianship of marriage over a minor girl, even if she is a thayyib (non-virgin), because the cause (minority) is the same type as the cause in the original case (minority). The Shafi'i position that virginity is the cause is refuted. For the second type (unity in genus): frequent tawaf is the cause for removing the hardship of impurity in the cat's leftover, and this same cause (frequent tawaf) also removes the hardship of seeking permission for slaves, because both hardships are of the same genus (hardship), though they differ in species. The passage then discusses the concept of 'tajnis al-illa' (generalizing the cause) using the example of guardianship over property and person: the cause is the minor's inability to manage affairs, which is a general meaning (jins) that applies to both property and person, so guardianship is established for both. The commentary notes the difference between zawaal (removal) of guardianship at puberty, and stresses that the cause can be expressed in various ways. The text also mentions a debate about whether a non-existent (adami) can be a cause, with Hanafi authorities like al-Dabusi and Fakhr al-Islam rejecting it, while later scholars like Ibn al-Humam following them.

Key Terms
القياس الشرعي (al-qiyas al-shar'i): Legal analogy: applying a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause ('illa).
تجنيس العلة (tajnis al-'illa): Generalizing the cause to a broader genus (jins) so that it applies to multiple species (anwa') of rulings.
اتحاد في الجنس (ittihad fi al-jins): Unity in genus: two rulings share a common genus (e.g., hardship) but differ in species (e.g., hardship of impurity vs. hardship of seeking permission).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, what is the cause ('illa) for the removal of hardship of impurity in the cat's leftover?
A) The cat's nature
B) Frequent tawaf (circumambulation)
C) The type of animal
D) The impurity itself

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, qiyas does not require exact identity of the cause; a shared genus suffices to transfer the ruling.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Two Types of Qiyas and the Necessity of Tajnis al-Illa
Defines and illustrates two types of qiyas with tajnis al-illa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two types of qiyas in Hanafi usul, identify when tajnis al-illa is required, and apply the condition to evaluate the validity of an analogy.

Core Idea
A valid qiyas requires the cause (illa) to be generic, covering both original and branch in a common genus.

In this passage from Usul al-Shashi, the author distinguishes two types of analogical reasoning (qiyas). The first type is valid when the cause is generic (tajnisi), while the second is invalid due to a specific difference (al-farq al-khas). Understanding this distinction is crucial for constructing sound analogies in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of qiyas
Read the passage and note that the first type involves a cause that is generic (tajnisi), while the second type lacks this generic quality.
The first type is also called qiyas al-illa al-tajnisi; the second is sometimes termed qiyas al-illa al-khassah.
2
Examine the example of father's guardianship
The author uses the father's guardianship over a minor: minority (sighar) is the cause. Guardianship over property and person are of the same genus but different species. This illustrates the first type when the cause is made generic.
The phrase 'من جنس تلك الولاية لا من نوعها' indicates genus-level similarity.
3
Determine the requirement for the first type
The passage states: 'لا بد في هذا النوع من القياس من تجنيس العلة' — it is necessary to make the cause generic. This means the illa must produce a ruling of the same genus in both original and branch.
Tajnis al-illa is a condition for validity.
4
Analyze the invalidity of the second type
The second type is invalid due to mumana'at al-tajnis (prevention of making the cause generic) and al-farq al-khas (specific difference). The effect of minority on property guardianship is greater than on person guardianship, so the cause does not operate uniformly.
A specific difference that breaks the genus-level similarity invalidates the analogy.
5
Apply the criterion to a new scenario
Consider a hypothetical: can we analogize from the permissibility of selling alcohol to non-Muslims to selling pork? The cause (darura or need) would need to be generic. If not, the analogy is invalid.
Use the concept of tajnis al-illa to test.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل القياس الشرعي لان حرج النجاسة غير حرج الاستيذان. وكذلك الصغر علة ولاية التصرف للاب. وهي الصغر وهذه الولاية من جنس تلك الولاية لا من نوعها. وإن بلوغ الجارية عن عقل علة زوال ولاية الاب في المال فيزول ولايته في حق النفس بهذه العلة، ثم لا بد في هذا النوع من القياس من تجنيس العلة بأن تقول: إنما يثبت ولاية الاب في مال الصغيرة؛ لانها عاجزة عن التصرف بنفسها فاثبت الشرع ولاية الاب كيلا يتعطل مصالحها المتعلقة بذلك وقد عجزت عن التصرف في نفسها فوجب القول بولاية الاب عليها، وعلى هذا نظائره، وحكم القياس الاول: ان لا يبطل بالفرق؛ لان الاصل مع الفرع لما اتحد في العلة وجب اتحادهما في الحكم وان افترقا في غير هذه العلة، وحكم القياس الثاني: فساده بممانعة التجنيس والفرق الخاص وهو بيان ان تاثير الصغر في ولاية التصرف في المال فوق تاثيره في ولاية التصرف في النفس
Section on Analogical Reasoning. Because the hardship of impurity is not the hardship of seeking permission. Likewise, minority is the cause of guardianship of disposition for the father. It is minority, and this guardianship is of the genus of that guardianship, not of its type. And the reaching of puberty with reason of the girl is the cause of the removal of the father's guardianship over property, so his guardianship over the person ceases by this cause. Then, in this type of analogy, it is necessary to make the cause generic by saying: The father's guardianship over the minor's property is established because she is incapable of managing herself, so the Law established the father's guardianship so that her interests related to that do not become neglected. And since she is incapable of managing herself, it is necessary to say that the father has guardianship over her. And likewise its parallels. And the ruling of the first type of analogy is that it is not invalidated by a difference, because the original and the branch, when they are united in the cause, their union in the ruling is necessary even if they differ in other than this cause. And the ruling of the second type of analogy is its invalidity due to the prevention of making the cause generic and the specific difference, which is the explanation that the effect of minority on guardianship over property is greater than its effect on guardianship over the person.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi explains the two types of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul. The first type is where the cause (illa) is generic (tajnisi), meaning it applies to both the original (asl) and the branch (far') in a common genus of ruling. An example given is the father's guardianship over a minor daughter: the cause is 'incapacity to manage affairs' which applies both to property (mal) and to the person (nafs), so the ruling of guardianship extends to both. The second type is where the cause is not generic; the ruling in the branch is of a different genus, and the specific difference (farq khas) invalidates the analogy. The passage emphasizes that in the first type, mere differences between original and branch do not break the analogy, while in the second type, the analogy is invalid because the cause does not cover both rulings uniformly.

Key Terms
القياس الشرعي (al-qiyas al-shar'i): Analogical reasoning in Islamic jurisprudence, comparing a new case (far') to an original case (asl) due to a shared cause (illa).
تجنيس العلة (tajnis al-illa): Making the cause generic so that it covers a common genus of rulings between original and branch.
الفرق الخاص (al-farq al-khas): A specific difference that prevents the analogy because it shows the cause does not operate uniformly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What invalidates the second type of qiyas according to the passage?
A) The original and branch differ in any attribute.
B) The cause is not generic, leading to a specific difference (al-farq al-khas).
C) The cause is hidden.
D) The branch contradicts the original.

Key Takeaway
The validity of qiyas depends on the cause being generic (tajnisi); a specific difference that prevents the genus from covering both rulings invalidates the analogy.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Three Types of Qiyas and Their Basic Rulings
Explains the three types of qiyas and rulings for each

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of qiyas (explicit cause, indicated cause, derived cause) and state the ruling for each type according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Qiyas is of three types: with explicit cause, with indicated cause, and with derived cause; each has a distinct ruling on validity.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi classifies qiyas into three categories based on how the cause (illa) is known. Understanding this classification is essential for correctly applying analogical reasoning in deriving legal rulings. We will examine each type and its ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types
Read the passage and list the three types of qiyas mentioned: qiyas with explicit cause (first), qiyas with cause indicated by dalala (second), and qiyas with cause derived by ijtihad (third).
The first type is based on an explicit textual cause; the second on an implied cause; the third on a cause derived by reasoning.
2
State the ruling for the first type
The passage states: 'Hukm al-qiyas al-awwal: an la yubtil bi al-farq' – the first type is not invalidated by a general difference between asl and far'.
Unity in cause overrides differences in attributes.
3
State the ruling for the second type
The second type is corrupted by prevention of generalization (mumana'at al-tajnis) or by a specific difference (farq khas) that shows the cause is not effective in the branch.
Even if the cause is indicated, a specific difference can break the analogy.
4
State the ruling for the third type
The third type (qiyas bi-illa mustanbitah) is valid provided the attribute is suitable (munasib) and the ruling is attributed to it due to suitability, not because the Shari'ah explicitly designated it as a cause.
Suitability (munasaba) is the key condition.
5
Note the condition for the third type
The condition is that the attribute (wasf) must necessitate the ruling by its nature and be associated with the ruling in a text or consensus.
Example: minority as cause for guardianship because it implies inability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

والمعروض من حيث هو كذلك، واعلم أن في هذا المقام أي: في مقام الفرق بين القياسين ببطلان الثاني بالفرق الخاص إشكال من وجوه : الأول: أن تعليل الماتن في القياس الأول بأن الاتحاد في العلة يوجب الاتحاد في الحكم يشترك فيه القسمان فلم قيد النوع الأوّل بذلك التعليل، والثاني : أنّ الفرق إذا كان في المعنى المؤثر يبطل بـــه القـسمان أي: الأوّل والثاني بالقياس وإذا كان في غيره لا يضر لا بالأوّل ولا بالثاني والثالث: أن المذكور إذا تقرر لا نسلّم القسم الأوّل عن الخلل أيضاً كما لا نسلّم القسم الثاني، فما الفائدة في تخصيص الثاني؟ والجواب الأول: أنّ الاتحاد على نوعين: اتحاد في النوع واتحاد في الجنس، والمراد هاهنا الاتحاد في النوع ولا شكّ أنّ الاتحاد في العلة لا يوجب الاتحاد النوعي في القسم الثاني، وعن الثاني: أنّ الفرق في المعنى المؤثر غير متصوّر كما ترى ولذا قيد بقوله: «في غير هذه العلة» بخلاف القسم الثاني فإن الفرق في المعنى المؤثر متوهم، وعن الثالث: أنّ الفرق الخاص المذكور غير متقرّر فلا يرد الإشكال غاية ما في الباب أنّ الماتن رحمه الله لم يتعرّض لهذا الفرق في القسم الأوّل؛ لأنه غير متوهم بخلاف القسم الثاني، فإنّه متوهم فافهم، كذا في "شرح المنار" وحواشيه. ١٢ (۱) قوله: [بالنظر إليه ] أي: ظاهراً وإنما قال: «بالنظر إليه» ظاهراً؛ لأنّ ثبوت تحقيق العلة في القياس ليس بقطعي، بل نقول: إنّ هذا الوصف علّة نظراً إلى الظاهر؛ لأنّ كلامنا فيما لم تكن العلة صةً. ۱۲ (۲) قوله: [يضاف الحكم إليه جواب إذا أي: إذا وجدنا مناسباً للحكم وقد اقترن به الحكم في موضـــع آخر من نص أو إجماع يضاف الحكم إلى ذلك الوصف كذا في "معدن الأصول". ١٢ (۳) قوله: [لا لشهادة الشرع بكونه ] أي: بكون الوصف علّة كما إذا علّلنا في ولاية الإنكاح في الصغير بعلة الصغر للمناسبة؛ لأنّ ولاية الإنكاح لم تشرع إلاّ على وجه النظر للصغير باعتبار عجـــزه عـــــن مباشرة النكاح مع حاجة إلى مقصوده والصغير مورث للعجز فكان هذا تعليلاً بوصف ملائم للحكم منصوصة. ١٢

Thus in Ma'din al-Usul. 12 (3) His saying: [not because of Shari'ah testimony that it is] meaning that the attribute is a cause, as when we give the cause for guardianship of marriage for a minor by the cause of minority for suitability; because guardianship of marriage was legislated only for the sake of looking after the minor due to his inability to directly perform the marriage with need for its objective, and minority causes inability, so this is a reasoning with an attribute suitable for the ruling that is stipulated. 12
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage from Al-Shashi's Usul, with the hashia Ahsan al-Hawashi, explains the classification of qiyas (analogical deduction) into three types and the rulings for each. The first type is qiyas where the cause (illa) is explicitly mentioned in the text; its ruling is that it is not invalidated by a general difference (farq) between the original (asl) and branch (far'), because unity in the cause requires unity in the ruling, even if they differ in other attributes. The second type is qiyas where the cause is derived by indication (dalala) from the text; its ruling is that it is corrupted by prevention of the generalization of the cause (mumana'at al-tajnis) or by a specific difference (farq khas) that shows the cause is not effective in the branch. An example is given: the effect of minority (sighar) on guardianship of property is stronger than on guardianship of self, leading to a discussion of the third type. The third type is qiyas with a cause derived by opinion and ijtihad (mustanbitah), applicable to all other ijtihadi issues. Its condition is that the attribute must be suitable (munasib) for the ruling, meaning that if we find an attribute that necessitates the ruling by its nature and has been associated with the ruling in a place of consensus or text, the ruling is attributed to that attribute due to suitability (munasaba), not because the Shari'ah explicitly designated it as a cause. An example is given of marriage guardianship for a minor, where minority is taken as the cause because it leads to inability, and the ruling is attributed to it due to suitability. The passage then addresses potential objections about the difference between the first and second types, clarifying that the first type's cause is textually indicated, while the second's is inferred, and the specific difference only invalidates the second because it raises doubt about the cause's effectiveness. The commentary emphasizes that the third type's cause is based on ijtihad and is not definitive, but is valid in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical deduction: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared cause (illa).
علة مستنبطة (illa mustanbitah): A cause derived by ijtihad and opinion, not explicitly stated in the text or consensus.
الوصف المناسب (al-wasf al-munasib): An attribute that is suitable for the ruling, meaning it necessitates the ruling by its nature and has been associated with it in a text or consensus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for the second type of qiyas (with indicated cause) according to the passage?
A) It is never invalidated by any difference.
B) It is corrupted by a specific difference (farq khas) or prevention of generalization.
C) It is only valid if the cause is explicit.
D) It is invalid per se.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is classified into three types based on how the cause is known, and each type has distinct rules for validity.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Qiyas with Derived Cause: Condition of Suitability
Focuses on the third type of qiyas and its condition of suitability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the condition of suitability (munasaba) for qiyas with a derived cause (illa mustanbitah) and apply it to a fiqh example.

Core Idea
For qiyas with a derived cause, the attribute must be suitable (munasib) and the ruling must be attributed to it due to that suitability, not because the Shari'ah explicitly designated it as a cause.

This passage introduces the third type of qiyas, which is the most commonly used for novel issues. The key condition is that the attribute chosen as the cause must be 'suitable' (munasib) – meaning it naturally necessitates the ruling and has been associated with that ruling in a text or consensus. We will explore this condition and its application through the example of marriage guardianship for a minor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the third type and its condition
Locate in the passage the definition of the third type: 'القياس بعلة مستنبطة بالرأي والاجتهاد'. Then find the condition: 'إذا وجدنا وصفا مناسبا للحكم ... يضاف الحكم إليه للمناسبة'.
The attribute is not declared a cause by the Lawgiver but is considered cause due to its suitability.
2
Understand 'suitability' (munasaba)
Suitability means the attribute logically or rationally demands the ruling. For example, minority (sighar) causes inability, and inability calls for guardianship.
The attribute must be 'مناسب' – appropriate and relevant.
3
Examine the example: marriage guardianship
The passage gives the example of a minor girl's marriage. Minority is taken as the cause (illa) for guardianship because it leads to inability, which is the rationale behind guardianship. This is reasoning with a suitable attribute.
The example shows how the condition is fulfilled.
4
Analyze the dispute about this type
The passage includes a madhhab dispute on the validity of qiyas with a derived cause. Some schools only accept explicit causes. The Hanafi position is that it is valid if the attribute is suitable and associated with the ruling.
This dispute is reflected in the al_mukhtalaf_fih block below.
5
Apply to a new case
Think of a contemporary issue, such as the permissibility of a new financial transaction. Find a suitable attribute that is linked to a known ruling in texts.
Practice using the condition.

Commentary
This passage from Al-Shashi's Usul, with the hashia Ahsan al-Hawashi, explains the classification of qiyas (analogical deduction) into three types and the rulings for each. The first type is qiyas where the cause (illa) is explicitly mentioned in the text; its ruling is that it is not invalidated by a general difference (farq) between the original (asl) and branch (far'), because unity in the cause requires unity in the ruling, even if they differ in other attributes. The second type is qiyas where the cause is derived by indication (dalala) from the text; its ruling is that it is corrupted by prevention of the generalization of the cause (mumana'at al-tajnis) or by a specific difference (farq khas) that shows the cause is not effective in the branch. An example is given: the effect of minority (sighar) on guardianship of property is stronger than on guardianship of self, leading to a discussion of the third type. The third type is qiyas with a cause derived by opinion and ijtihad (mustanbitah), applicable to all other ijtihadi issues. Its condition is that the attribute must be suitable (munasib) for the ruling, meaning that if we find an attribute that necessitates the ruling by its nature and has been associated with the ruling in a place of consensus or text, the ruling is attributed to that attribute due to suitability (munasaba), not because the Shari'ah explicitly designated it as a cause. An example is given of marriage guardianship for a minor, where minority is taken as the cause because it leads to inability, and the ruling is attributed to it due to suitability. The passage then addresses potential objections about the difference between the first and second types, clarifying that the first type's cause is textually indicated, while the second's is inferred, and the specific difference only invalidates the second because it raises doubt about the cause's effectiveness. The commentary emphasizes that the third type's cause is based on ijtihad and is not definitive, but is valid in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
علة مستنبطة (illa mustanbitah): A cause derived by ijtihad and opinion, not explicitly stated in the text or consensus.
الوصف المناسب (al-wasf al-munasib): An attribute that is suitable for the ruling, meaning it necessitates the ruling by its nature and has been associated with it in a text or consensus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for the validity of the third type of qiyas according to the passage?
A) The cause must be explicitly mentioned in the Quran or Sunnah.
B) The attribute must be suitable and the ruling attributed to it for suitability, provided the attribute has been associated with the ruling in a text or consensus.
C) The cause must be derived from the consensus of the Companions only.
D) The qiyas must be based on a cause that is general in all aspects.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas with a derived cause is valid in Hanafi usul provided the attribute is suitable and textually/consensually linked to the ruling.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Distinction Between First and Second Types: Objections and Answers
Discusses objections and answers regarding the distinction between first and second types of qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the distinction between the first and second types of qiyas and analyze the objections raised against the author's classification.

Core Idea
The first type of qiyas is not invalidated by a specific difference because the cause is explicit, while the second type is invalidated because a specific difference is conceivable.

The passage includes a sophisticated discussion of potential objections to the classification of the first two types of qiyas. It clarifies that the first type's unity of cause ensures unity of ruling even with differences, while the second type's cause is not explicit, making it vulnerable to specific differences that break the analogy. This lesson will walk through the objections and their answers.

Guided Path
1
Recall the first and second types
Reread the definitions: first type has an explicit cause; second type has a cause indicated by the text but not explicit. Their rulings differ: first is not invalidated by any difference; second is invalidated by a specific difference (farq khas).
The specific difference is a difference in an effective meaning that shows the cause is not operative in the branch.
2
Identify the objections
The passage lists three objections: 1) The reasoning that unity in cause necessitates unity in ruling applies to both types, so why limit it to the first? 2) If a difference is in the effective meaning, it should invalidate both types; if not, it should harm neither. 3) The first type might also be defective, so why single out the second?
These objections test the consistency of the classification.
3
Follow the answers
The answers: 1) Unity in type (not just genus) is required; the second type may have only unity in genus, not in type. 2) A difference in effective meaning is inconceivable in the first type because the cause is explicit and determines the ruling; in the second it is conceivable. 3) The specific difference mentioned for the second type is not established for the first, so no inconsistency.
The key concept: the first type's cause is certain, so no specific difference can negate it; the second type's cause is probable, so a specific difference can refute it.
4
Understand the epistemological underpinning
The passage notes that the verification of the cause in qiyas is not definitive (qat'i) but apparent (zahir). This is especially true for the second and third types. The first type's explicit cause gives it more strength.
See the footnote: 'ثبوت تحقيق العلة في القياس ليس بقطعي'.
5
Apply the distinction
When analyzing a qiyas, first determine if the cause is explicit or indicated. If explicit, a general difference does not harm; if indicated, check for any specific difference that would break the analogy.
This practical rule helps in evaluating arguments.

Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage from Al-Shashi's Usul, with the hashia Ahsan al-Hawashi, explains the classification of qiyas (analogical deduction) into three types and the rulings for each. The first type is qiyas where the cause (illa) is explicitly mentioned in the text; its ruling is that it is not invalidated by a general difference (farq) between the original (asl) and branch (far'), because unity in the cause requires unity in the ruling, even if they differ in other attributes. The second type is qiyas where the cause is derived by indication (dalala) from the text; its ruling is that it is corrupted by prevention of the generalization of the cause (mumana'at al-tajnis) or by a specific difference (farq khas) that shows the cause is not effective in the branch. An example is given: the effect of minority (sighar) on guardianship of property is stronger than on guardianship of self, leading to a discussion of the third type. The third type is qiyas with a cause derived by opinion and ijtihad (mustanbitah), applicable to all other ijtihadi issues. Its condition is that the attribute must be suitable (munasib) for the ruling, meaning that if we find an attribute that necessitates the ruling by its nature and has been associated with the ruling in a place of consensus or text, the ruling is attributed to that attribute due to suitability (munasaba), not because the Shari'ah explicitly designated it as a cause. An example is given of marriage guardianship for a minor, where minority is taken as the cause because it leads to inability, and the ruling is attributed to it due to suitability. The passage then addresses potential objections about the difference between the first and second types, clarifying that the first type's cause is textually indicated, while the second's is inferred, and the specific difference only invalidates the second because it raises doubt about the cause's effectiveness. The commentary emphasizes that the third type's cause is based on ijtihad and is not definitive, but is valid in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
الفرق الخاص (al-farq al-khas): A specific difference that pertains to the effective meaning (ma'na mu'aththir), which can invalidate a qiyas of the second type.
المعنى المؤثر (al-ma'na al-mu'aththir): The effective meaning: the attribute that actually influences the ruling. A difference in this meaning can break the analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a specific difference (farq khas) only a concern for the second type of qiyas and not the first?
A) Because the first type's cause is explicit, making a specific difference in the effective meaning inconceivable.
B) Because the first type's cause is general, so all differences are irrelevant.
C) Because the second type's cause is always textually indicated, so it is weak.
D) Because the author did not discuss the first type.

Key Takeaway
The first type of qiyas (explicit cause) is immune to specific differences, while the second type (indicated cause) is not, due to the certainty vs. probability of the cause.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
The Third Type of Qiyas: Qiyas with an Inferred Cause
Defining qiyas with inferred cause and its conditions for validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qiyas with an inferred cause, identify its conditions, and apply the test of relevant difference (farq munasib) to invalidate a faulty analogy.

Core Idea
A suitable description conjoined with a ruling creates strong presumption, but must show effect elsewhere to necessitate action.

In this passage, Usul al-Shashi introduces the third type of analogy, where the cause is not stated but inferred through reasoning. You will learn the precise conditions that make this qiyas valid and how a relevant difference between the original and branch can break the analogy. The discussion includes a classic Hanafi–Shafi‘i dispute over zakat on a minor’s property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of qiyas
Recognize that this is qiyas where the cause is inferred by personal ijtihad, not explicitly mentioned.
Distinguish from qiyas with an explicit cause (jali) or obvious cause.
2
Analyze the condition of suitability and conjunction
Look for the phrase 'وصف مناسب للحكم وقد اقترن به الحكم في موضع الإجماع'. Suitability alone is insufficient; the ruling must be conjoined with the description in a text or consensus.
3
Understand strong presumption (ghalabat al-ẓann)
The conjunction creates a strong presumption that the description is the cause. In Hanafi usul, this obligates action when no stronger evidence exists.
It is not certainty; compare to the traveler who cannot perform tayammum despite strong presumption.
4
Apply the requirement of effect manifestation
The passage states that the description must show its effect in another place (e.g., guardianship of property for a minor). This distinguishes permissive suitability from obligatory necessity.
Mere suitability permits analogy; manifestation of effect necessitates it.
5
Test with a relevant difference (al-farq al-munāsib)
If another suitable description is found in the original that contradicts the first, the presumption is lost. Practice with the zakat on minor example.
The Hanafi response: the cause is purification, absent in the minor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل القياس الشرعي
النفس وبيان القسم الثالث : وهو القياس بعلة مستنبطة بالرأي والاجتهاد في سائر المسائل القياسية الاجتهادية. ظاهر، وتحقيق ذلك إذا وجدنا وصفا مناسبا للحكم وهو بحال يوجب ثبوت الحكم ويتقاضاه بالنظر إليه وقد اقترن به الحكم في موضع الإجماع يضاف الحكم إليه للمناسبة لا لشهادة الشرع بكونه علة، ونظيره إذا رأينا شخصا أعطى فقيرا درهما غلب على الظن أن الإعطاء لدفع حاجة الفقير وتحصيل مصالح الثواب، إذا عرف هذا فنقول: إذا رأينا وصفا مناسبا للحكم وقد اقترن به الحكم في موضع الإجماع يغلب الظن بإضافة الحكم إلى ذلك الوصف وغلبة الظن في الشرع توجب العمل عند انعدام ما فوقها من الدليل، وهو بمنزلة المسافر إذا غلب على ظنه أن بقربه ماء لم يجز له التيمم، وعلى هذا مسائل التحري، وحكم هذا القياس أن يبطل بالفرق المناسب؛ لأنه إذا وجد مناسب سواه في صورة الحكم فلا يبقى الظن بإضافة الحكم إليه فلا يثبت الحكم به؛ لأنه كان بناء على غلبة الظن وقد بطل ذلك بالفرق، وقد ظهر أثر هذا الوصف في موضع الإجماع وهو ولاية المال، فإنها ثابتة في مال الصغير بالإجماع وإنما يشترط هذا لوجوب العمل بالوصف؛ لأن الوصف في القياس بمنزلة الشاهد وهو اجتنابه عن محظورات دينه واجتنابه عنها يدل ظاهرا على أنه يجتنب عن الكذب في الشهادة أيضا فظهور أثر لوصف في موضع آخر يدل ظاهرا على أنه مؤثر في موضع النزاع فهذا يوجب العمل بالقياس بهذه العلة، وأما مجرد المناسبة فيجوزه ولا يوجبه، كذا في الفصول والمعدن.
(قوله: [لم يجز له التيمم] لأن غلبة الظن عند انعدام ما فوقها من الدليل بمنزلة المتحقق.
قوله: [مسائل التحري] كما إذا اجتهبت عليه القبلة وتحر ووقع تحريه على شيء بغلبة الظن وليس من يسأله فيجب العمل به.
قوله: [بالفرق المناسب] أي: بالفرق بين الأصل والفرع في الوصف المناسب؛ لأن عنده وجود الفرق يوجد مناسب في المقيس عليه سوى الوصف الذي عللتموه، ومثال ذلك كما قال الشافعي رحمه الله: يجب الزكاة في مال الصبي قياسا على البالغ والجامع دفع حاجة الفقير، وللسائل أن يبطل بالفرق يقول: إن وجوب الزكاة في صورة موضع الإجماع لتطهير الآثام والذنوب وهذا المعنى مفقود في صورة الفرع فلا يجب، كذا في الفصول والمعدن.
Chapter on legal analogy. The third type: analogy with a cause inferred by opinion and ijtihad in all analogical matters subject to ijtihad. The explanation: when we find a description suitable for the ruling and it is such that it necessitates the ruling and demands it by its very consideration, and the ruling is conjoined with it in a place of consensus, the ruling is attributed to that description due to suitability, not because the Law attests to it being the cause. Its analogy: if we see a person give a dirham to a poor person, it is strongly thought that the giving is to fulfill the poor person's need and to obtain the benefits of reward. Once this is known, we say: when we find a description suitable for the ruling and the ruling is conjoined with it in a place of consensus, a strong presumption arises that the ruling is attached to that description, and a strong presumption in the Law necessitates action in the absence of proof above it. It is like the traveler who strongly believes water is near, but it is not permissible for him to perform tayammum. On this basis are the cases of ijtihad (taharrī). The ruling of this analogy is that it is invalidated by a relevant difference because if another suitable description is found in the case of the ruling, the strong presumption of attaching the ruling to the first description no longer remains, so the ruling is not established by it, as it was based on strong presumption and that presumption is nullified by the difference. And the effect of this description has appeared in the place of consensus, namely the guardianship of property, for it is established in the property of a minor by consensus. This condition is required for the necessity of acting upon the description, because the description in analogy is like a witness: his avoidance of forbidden things in his religion indicates that he also avoids lying in testimony. So the appearance of the effect of a description in another place indicates that it is effective in the disputed place, and this necessitates acting upon the analogy with this cause. Mere suitability permits it but does not necessitate it, as stated in al-Fusul and al-Ma'din. (His saying: 'it is not permissible for him to perform tayammum' because strong presumption in the absence of proof above it is like certainty. His saying: 'cases of ijtihad' like when one exerts himself for the qibla and his ijtihad falls upon something with strong presumption and there is no one to ask, then he must act upon it. His saying: 'by the relevant difference' meaning by the difference between the original and the branch in the suitable description, because according to him, the existence of the difference indicates that there is another suitable description in the original apart from the one you relied upon. An example is as al-Shafi'i said: Zakat is obligatory on the property of a minor by analogy with an adult, and the common link is the relief of the poor person's need. The opponent can invalidate it by the difference, saying that the obligation of zakat in the case of consensus is to purify sins and offences, and this meaning is absent in the branch case, so it is not obligatory, as in al-Fusul and al-Ma'din.)
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi, with commentary from Ahsan al-Hawashi, defines the third type of qiyas: qiyas with a cause inferred by personal reasoning and ijtihad (al-qiyas bi-illah mustanbiṭah bi al-ra'y wa al-ijtihad). The author first states the definition, then elaborates on its condition: we find a description (waṣf) that is suitable (munāsib) for a ruling, and that ruling is conjoined with that description in a place of consensus (ijma) or a text (nass). When that happens, we attribute the ruling to that description due to suitability, not because the Law explicitly states it is the cause. The author provides an analogy: if we see someone give a dirham to a poor person, we presume it is to alleviate need and gain reward. Similarly, when we see a suitable description conjoined with a ruling in a consensus, we form a strong presumption (ghalabat al-ẓann) that the ruling is attached to that description. This strong presumption obligates action in the absence of stronger evidence. The author compares it to a traveler who strongly believes water is near but cannot perform tayammum because the presumption is not certainty. This type of qiyas is invalidated by a suitable difference (al-farq al-munāsib) between the original and the branch. If another suitable description exists in the original, the presumption is lost and the ruling does not hold. The author illustrates with the example of zakat on a minor's property: al-Shafi'i analogizes from an adult, citing the common link of relieving the poor, but the Hanafi response is that the cause is purification of sins, which is absent in the minor, so the analogy fails. The commentary emphasizes that the condition of the description showing its effect in another place is necessary for it to necessitate action; mere suitability permits analogy but does not require it.

Key Terms
القياس بعلة مستنبطة (al-qiyās bi-‘illah mustanbiṭah): Analogy with a cause inferred by the mujtahid's reasoning and ijtihad, not explicitly stated in the Law
الوصف المناسب (al-waṣf al-munāsib): A description that is suitable for the ruling, meaning it is conducive to the wisdom behind the ruling
غلب الظن (ghalabat al-ẓann): Strong presumption that arises when a suitable description is conjoined with a ruling in a text or consensus
الفرق المناسب (al-farq al-munāsib): A relevant difference between the original and branch that shows the description is not the cause in the branch

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what invalidates qiyas with an inferred cause?
A) Insufficient suitability of the description.
B) A relevant difference between the original and the branch.
C) Absence of consensus on the original case.
D) The description not being explicitly stated as the cause in the Law.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas with an inferred cause requires the description to be suitable, conjoined with the ruling, and to have manifested its effect elsewhere; a relevant difference invalidates it.

Three Categories of 'Illah in Qiyas
Explaining three categories of legal cause in qiyas with witness analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of 'illah (legal cause) in Hanafi qiyas based on their source of proof (nass, ijma', ijtihad) and explain their relative strength using the witness testimony analogy.

Core Idea
The strength of a legal cause in qiyas depends on its source: text, consensus, or ijtihad — analogous to levels of witness certification.

In Hanafi legal theory, not all causes for analogy are created equal. This lesson from Usul al-Shashi classifies the 'illah (legal cause) into three categories, each with its own evidentiary weight. The author uses a vivid analogy to witness testimony to clarify their hierarchy. Understanding this classification is key to evaluating the strength of rulings derived through qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Extract from the passage the three types of 'illah: (1) known from the Quran and Sunnah, (2) known by consensus (ijma'), and (3) known by ijtihad and opinion (ra'y).
The text calls these 'the three categories' and contrasts them.
2
Map the witness analogy
For each category, identify its counterpart in witness testimony: Type 1 is like a witness certified by a certifier (muzakki); Type 2 is like a witness with apparent uprightness before certification; Type 3 is like a witness of unknown character (mastur).
The strength decreases from Type 1 to Type 3.
3
Analyze the distinction between Type 2 and Type 3
Note the objection that Type 2 and Type 3 seem similar. Understand the author's response: Type 2 is proven by general consensus (ijma' al-ummah), while Type 3 relies on the opponent's acceptance or a specific consensus with the proponent. The difference is in principle even if not always in practice.
This highlights the nuanced epistemology of 'illah.
4
Assess the binding nature of each type
Type 1 is absolutely binding (qat'i). Type 2 is also binding but slightly weaker. Type 3 becomes binding only when the ruling is associated with it in a place of consensus (making it effectively Type 2). Otherwise, it is permissible (not obligatory) to act upon it if the opponent does not object.
This affects the weight of arguments in juristic debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Principles of al-Shashi with excellent footnotes. That is, what we mentioned of the three categories and the difference between them. And it is the description known by the Book and the Sunnah. Regarding justice. Chapter on legal qiyas from those who certify. This, acting upon the first type is like ruling by testimony after certifying the witness, i.e., the witness. Acting upon the type. And his modification, and the second type is like testimony when justice appears before certification, acting upon the type etc. And the third type is like testimony of one whose status is unknown. And it is a description known by opinion and ijtihad. (1) His saying: 'was al-'amal' means upon what we mentioned of the three categories and the difference between them, that the description known by the Book and the Sunnah is like the certification of the witness who is declared upright by the certifier; because the indication of the text that it is a cause is like the certification of the witness by the certifier. And the description known by consensus is like the witness whose uprightness appeared before certification; because consensus does not indicate explicitly nor by implication that this description is its cause. (2) His saying: [by the first type] it is the cause stated explicitly in the Qur'an and Hadith, like a judgment based on the testimony of witnesses after their modification, then their certification by the testimony of certifiers; for it cannot be imagined to be overturned at all, and it is a complete, firm, and solid judgment that cannot admit invalidation or revocation. (3) His saying: [like testimony of one whose status is unknown] because his uprightness and corruption have not appeared, just as it has not appeared that the description is a cause by a proof from text or consensus. If you say: Acting upon the third category is obligatory, as the author stated that overwhelming [probability] necessitates action, and it being like one whose status is unknown requires that acting upon it is not obligatory but permissible; because judgment based on testimony of one whose status is unknown is permissible if the opponent does not object to apparent uprightness. We say: Acting upon the appropriate description is obligatory only when the ruling is associated with it in a place of consensus, and it is of the second type. And someone may say: Thus there is no real difference between the second and third types. It is answered: By 'first consensus' is meant the consensus of the ummah, and by 'second' the consensus of the opponent with the proponent of the cause. And it is answered: The difference between the second and third types is established in principle, though not established in relation to [؟] and it is the association of the ruling with it in a place of consensus or in a place of text, and this suffices for the difference. Thus in 'al-Fusul'.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage from the hashia on Usul al-Shashi defines the three categories of 'illah (legal cause) used in qiyas, comparing them to types of witness testimony in court. The author explains that an 'illah known from the Quran or Sunnah is like a witness who has been certified by a certifier (muzakki) — it is strongest and cannot be overturned. An 'illah known by ijma' (consensus) is like a witness whose uprightness is apparent but not yet certified — it is strong but slightly weaker. An 'illah known by ijtihad and ra'y (opinion) is like a witness of unknown character — it is the weakest but still valid if accepted by the opponent. The hashia addresses a potential objection: if the third type is obligatory to act upon, why is it compared to an uncertified witness whose testimony is merely permissible? The response clarifies that the third type becomes obligatory only when the ruling is associated with it in a place of consensus, making it effectively the second type. The overall purpose is to establish the hierarchy of evidentiary strength in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
العلة (al-illah): The legal cause ('illah) in qiyas, which is the attribute that necessitates a ruling and is used to extend that ruling from the original case to a new case.
المزكي (al-muzakki): The certifier who testifies to the uprightness of a witness; used in the analogy to show that an 'illah known by text is certified directly by the Lawgiver.
المستور (al-mastur): A witness whose character is unknown (neither clearly upright nor corrupt); used as the analogy for the third type of 'illah (by ijtihad).
غلبة الظن (ghālib al-ẓann): Overwhelming probability; the level of certainty required for action on ijtihad-based 'illah according to the author.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the analogy used in this passage, which type of 'illah is compared to a witness who has been certified by a certifier (muzakki)?
A) The 'illah known by ijtihad and ra'y.
B) The 'illah known by ijma'.
C) The 'illah known by the Quran and Sunnah.
D) The 'illah that is suitable (munasib).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of 'illah into three categories based on source of proof establishes a hierarchy of evidentiary strength for qiyas, analogous to witness testimony.

The Eight Objections to Qiyas: An Overview
Listing eight objections and emphasizing mumana'a's primacy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight standard objections to qiyas in order and explain why al-mumana'a is the foundational objection.

Core Idea
Eight objections challenge qiyas; al-mumana'a is the first and most essential.

This passage from the Hanafi usul text introduces the eight objections that an opponent can raise against a qiyas argument. Understanding these objections is critical for both constructing and critiquing analogical reasoning. We will focus on the list and the special status of the first objection: al-mumana'a.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Eight Objections
Read the passage and extract the eight names: al-mumana'a, al-qawl bi-mujab al-'illah, al-qalb, al-'aks, fasad al-wad', al-farq, al-naqd, and al-mu'arada. Memorize them in order.
The order is important because it reflects the recommended sequence in debate.
2
Understand the Foundation of al-Mumana'a
The text states that al-mumana'a is 'the foundation of debate and its origin'. Reflect on why denial (similar to a defendant in court) is the first step.
Debate is modeled on litigation; the opponent's role is to deny first.
3
Recognize the Procedural Rule
The passage instructs that the opponent should not go beyond al-mumana'a except when the proponent's cause is established. Only then may other objections be used.
This ensures efficient debate: tackle the core denial first.
4
Preview the Two Types of al-Mumana'a
Note that al-mumana'a has two types: prevention of the description (man' al-wasf) and prevention of the ruling (man' al-hukm). The next lesson will detail them.
This sets the stage for deeper analysis.

(۱) قوله: [الممانعة] هي أساس المناظرة وأصلها؛ لأن المناظرة وضعت على مثال الخصومات في الدعاوي الواقعة في حقوق العبادة، فالمعلّل يدعي لزوم الحكم الذي رام قصد إثباته على السائل، والسائل يدعي عليه فكان سبيله الإنكار كما أن سبيل المدعى عليه في الحقوق الدفع عن نفسه والإنكار فلا ينبغي له أن يتجاوز إلى غير الممانعة إلا عند الضرورة وهي أنه إذا ثبت ما ادعاه المجيب مؤثراً في الحكم يتجاوز السائل عنها إلى القول بموجب العلة إن أمكنه ذلك بأن كان الوصف من جنس الحكم وإلا يشغل بالقلب ثم بالمعارضة، فإذا زال الكلام إلى المعارضة سهل الأمر على المجيب، كذا في 'الفصول'. (٦) قوله: [فلا يسقط بهلاك النصاب ... إلخ] جعل الشافعي رحمه الله وجوب مقدار الزكاه علته للحكم
Chapter on the objections directed against qiyas. There are eight objections: prevention, saying by the implication of the cause, reversal, inversion, corruption of placement, distinction, refutation, and counterargument. As for prevention, it is of two types: one is prevention of the description, and the second is prevention of the ruling. An example is in their saying: Zakat al-Fitr becomes obligatory by the evening of Fitr, so it is not void by his death on the night of Fitr. We say: We do not accept its obligation by the evening; rather, it becomes obligatory by the person. (1) His saying: [prevention] is the foundation of debate and its origin; because debate is modeled on litigation in claims concerning rights of worship. The proponent claims the bindingness of the ruling he intends to prove upon the opponent, and the opponent claims against him, so his way is denial, just as the way of the defendant in rights is to defend himself and deny. So he should not go beyond prevention except out of necessity, which is that if the claim of the respondent is established as effective in the ruling, the opponent goes beyond it to saying by the implication of the cause if he can, i.e., if the description is of the same genus as the ruling, otherwise he engages in reversal, then in counterargument. When the discussion shifts to counterargument, it becomes easy for the respondent. Thus in 'al-Fusul'. (2) His saying: [and distinction] And someone may say: He mentioned distinction but did not begin to give its example as he began in other objections. It is said: Because the example of distinction was mentioned in the previous chapter before this chapter, he did not mention it here for brevity, although it is possible that it was a scribal error in the copy of the text, and that is not unlikely. Thus in 'Ma'din al-Usul'. (3) His saying: [prevention of the description] is that he says: We do not accept that the description which the proponent made a cause exists in the disputed matter, and the prevention is either with a basis or without, and the basis is that on which the prevention is built. (4) His saying: [you support and are responsible for them] means the person responsible for his maintenance bears his expenses. And his saying: 'are responsible for them' means that person is in charge of that dependant, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Pay on behalf of those you support' i.e., you bear this expense for those whose expenses are upon you. So it is known by this that the dependant is a cause, and its verification will come in the chapter of causes from this book. (5) His saying: [and similarly] meaning like the prevention in the description in the previous issue, the prevention when he says: The amount of zakat which is five dirhams is obligatory in the liability, not tied to the property. Thus in 'al-Ma'din'. (6) His saying: [so it is not void by the destruction of the nisab... etc.] Al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) made the obligation of the amount of zakat a cause for the ruling...
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage from the hashia introduces the eight standard objections (as'ila) that can be raised against a qiyas argument in Hanafi usul. The objections are: al-mumana'a (prevention), al-qawl bi-mujab al-'illah (saying by the implication of the cause), al-qalb (reversal), al-'aks (inversion), fasad al-wad' (corruption of placement), al-farq (distinction), al-naqd (refutation), and al-mu'arada (counterargument). The focus here is on the first: mumana'a. It is divided into two types: prevention of the description (man' al-wasf) i.e., denying that the claimed 'illah actually exists in the original or branch case; and prevention of the ruling (man' al-hukm) i.e., denying the existence of the ruling in the original case. The text provides an example related to Zakat al-Fitr: the Shafi'i argues that Zakat al-Fitr is obligated by the arrival of the day of Fitr, so it does not fall by death before paying. The Hanafi responds by denying that the 'illah is the day; rather, it is the person (wealthy, free, resident). This is a prevention of the description. The hashia also explains that mumana'a is the foundational move in debate, analogous to a defendant denying a claim. It should be used first; only if the respondent's 'illah is established should the opponent move to other objections. The passage also clarifies that examples for 'farq' were omitted for brevity or possibly due to scribal error.

Key Terms
الممانعة (al-mumana'a): Prevention: an objection in qiyas where the opponent denies either the existence of the 'illah in the original case (man' al-wasf) or the existence of the ruling in the original case (man' al-hukm).
العلة (al-'illah): The cause or effective reason upon which the ruling in the original case is based, which the proponent seeks to extend to the new case.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a shared cause ('illah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first objection that the opponent (sail) should use against the proponent (mu'allil) in qiyas?
A) Al-qalb (reversal)
B) Al-mumana'a (prevention)
C) Al-mu'arada (counterargument)
D) Al-farq (distinction)

Key Takeaway
Al-mumana'a is the first and foundational objection in qiyas debate, divided into two types: prevention of the description and prevention of the ruling.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
